Zhabei

Water Cutoff in Huakang Lane Causes Dispute

In Huakang Lane, Huakang Road, Zhabei, there are dozens of bungalows owned by Tan Fuji, located at No. 4 Hanzhong Road. The monthly rent for each room is seven dollars and twenty cents, and the landlord provides tap water. Recently, for unknown reasons, a disagreement suddenly arose between the landlord and tenants. According to the tenants, the issue is related to house repairs. The houses were built in 1924, and all the tenants are long-time residents. Recently, some tenants requested the landlord to make repairs, but the landlord refused. The tenants then repaired the houses themselves and deducted the cost from the rent, which the landlord rejected, leading to the dispute. Yesterday, the tap water was cut off, causing panic among the tenants. They gathered to discuss the matter, and the sub-landlords Ji Ruyou, Li Rumao, Jiang Yuxin, Gui Buwang, Lü Zhaolong, Zhang Fengqi, Cheng Wanrong, Ma Jialian, Zhao Yuanji, Zhou Huaigen, and others decided to file a petition with the Fourth District Public Security Bureau, requesting assistance.

The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Expanding the Scope of Commercial Statistics

Since the Municipal Chamber of Commerce began conducting commercial statistics, it has successfully completed the financial industry and cotton cloth industry surveys, and published statistical compilations, which have been quite effective. The current Business Committee decided at yesterday's meeting to expand the scope of commercial statistics to conduct a general survey. Details are as follows:

Business Meeting. The current Business Committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce held its first meeting yesterday at 2 PM in the Municipal Chamber of Commerce meeting room. Those present were Guo Shun, Luo Qinghua, Li Wenjie, Zhang Nianxuan, Chen Ziming, Cheng Shujie, Chen Ziyi, Xu Xiaochu, Zhang Peizhen, Wang Jinshi, Ke Ganchen, Xue Guangqian, and others. Luo Qinghua chaired the meeting. The chairman first reported on (1) the re-appointment of committee members, (2) the commercial statistics conducted in the previous term, and (3) the principles for conducting commercial statistics in the future. Then, the following was discussed: (1) The four principles for conducting commercial statistics in the future. Resolution: Passed. The principles are as follows: (A) Select two or three major industrial and commercial sectors to begin with. "Start small and early, and avoid being comprehensive but slow." (B) Survey forms should be specifically designed based on the situation of each industry, rather than using general forms, to avoid "cutting the feet to fit the shoes." (C) Due to limited staff, the Chamber relies on the assistance of trade associations to conduct surveys. To encourage the interest of trade associations in the future, the Chamber should send commendation letters to trade associations that have performed well in surveys to encourage them. (D) In the future, survey data will be based on the year 1933 as the standard. (2) How to conduct commercial statistics in the future. Resolution: (A) The rice, coal, paper, electrical machinery, silk factory, and copper-iron machinery industries, which have been designated but not completed, must be completed within one month. (B) Designate the color printing, new medicine, and foreign sundry goods industries to start conducting statistics. (C) Send a letter to trade associations in other industries that have not been designated, requesting them to obtain survey forms from the Chamber and conduct general surveys and statistics within one week of receiving the letter. (D) Constantly monitor changes in the content of the completed statistics for the financial and cotton cloth industries for revision. (3) The four suggestions from the Business Section regarding the survey cases. Resolution: (1) and (3) can be implemented as is. (2) and (4) should be implemented based on the situation. (4) Discussion of the organizational charter of the Business Committee. Resolution: Passed and sent to the executive committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for record-keeping. (5) Setting the date for regular meetings. Resolution: To be held on the fourth Thursday of each month.

Organizational Charter. Organizational Charter of the Business Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce. (1) This charter is formulated in accordance with Article 3 of the general rules for committees of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. (2) The committee shall consist of fifteen to twenty-five members, nominated by the Standing Committee of the Chamber from among the member representatives and submitted to the Executive Committee for appointment, with one member designated as the director. (3) The duties of this committee are as follows: A. Design matters related to the improvement and development of industry and commerce. B. Plan for the improvement of industrial and commercial laws and regulations and the research of tariff rules. C. Assist the Business Section of the Chamber in matters related to industrial and commercial surveys and statistics, and mediation and arbitration of disputes. D. Handle other matters assigned by the Executive Committee and the Standing Committee of the Chamber. (4) The director shall chair the meetings of this committee. In the absence of the director, the attending members may elect one person as temporary chairman. (5) Decisions of this committee shall be made by a majority vote of the members present, with a quorum of more than half of the members. (6) Decisions of this committee shall be submitted to the Standing Committee for determination. (7) This committee shall meet at least once a month, convened by the director. Special meetings may be convened when necessary. (8) The detailed rules of procedure for this committee shall be formulated separately. (9) This charter shall be implemented upon approval by the Executive Committee, and the same shall apply to its amendments.

Shanghai County Storing Accumulated Grain in Warehouses

The Shanghai County Government, for the purpose of accumulating grain in the county, previously purchased land in the Second District to build warehouses, which have now been completed. All two thousand piculs of accumulated grain, previously handled by the Shanghai Soy and Rice Industry Association, have now been completely transported into the warehouses for storage. However, the provincial authorities previously instructed that the county's accumulated grain must be at least five thousand piculs. Seeing that the weather is dry and a famine has already formed, Magistrate Pan considers the accumulation of grain for disaster preparedness to be important. He is now finding ways to raise funds for further purchases. It is also reported that Shanghai County originally had assets, but with the division of the city and county, the county should receive 37%. The county government has sent a letter to the City and County Original Assets Management Committee to withdraw these funds for deposit in the treasury, in accordance with provincial orders.

Public Bus

Case of Liu Ansheng Crushed to Death

Changzhou Association Sends Letter Requesting Negotiation

The Changzhou Shanghai Association sent a letter to the Chinese Taxpayers' Committee and the Public Works Department regarding the tragic death of Liu Ansheng in a public bus accident, stating, "Respectfully, regarding the case of Mr. Tao Anren being injured by a public bus on August 7th, your committee's letter to the Public Works Department was heartfelt and deeply admired. It cited the past mistakes of the Public Works Department in protecting the British Public Bus Company, listing them one by one, and requesting measures to ensure the safety of citizens in the future, which is an essential proposal and a unanimous demand of the taxpayers. Unexpectedly, before the ink on your committee's letter to the Public Works Department was dry, Mr. Liu Ansheng, a member of our association from Changzhou, was tragically killed. According to a report from member Xie Ruichang, Liu Ansheng was from Changzhou, 21 years old, and worked at the Anglo-American Pharmacy on Shandong Road in the Public Concession. On August 7th at 10 PM, he was riding a bicycle, traveling south to north on Henan Road, in front of the Hongsheng South Goods Store and the Xiliangji Pharmacy. Public bus license number 15014, car number 253, traveling north to south, was speeding and recklessly driving, suddenly and unexpectedly, colliding head-on, causing Liu Ansheng to be unable to avoid it. The bicycle he was riding was caught in the front wheel of the public bus and dragged for more than ten feet. The wheel crushed Liu Ansheng's head, and his breastbone was shattered. He died from his injuries, and the bicycle was completely destroyed. Half an hour later, I learned of this and went to investigate. According to eyewitnesses as mentioned above, Liu Ansheng was sent to Renji Hospital, where he died. The police immediately sent him to the Feilun Road morgue for examination. I went to inquire, and the police instructed me to go the next day (August 8th). The next morning, I went with Liu Linsheng, the cousin of the deceased. At 10 AM, the examiner inquired, first the police and patrolmen stated that the public bus route was correct and that the deceased was careless. Then, the driver involved in the accident was asked, and he refused to admit that he had taken the wrong route. The patrolmen were not eyewitnesses at the time of the accident, how could they know whether the route was wrong? Later, Liu Linsheng, the cousin of the deceased, was asked, he was a worker, and he could not help but cry during the answer. The examiner asked if there were any witnesses. He replied that there was a relative, Xie Ruichang, who had gone to the scene half an hour after the accident to inquire. According to eyewitnesses at the time, the public bus was traveling too fast, had gone outside the prescribed route, and did not honk the horn to warn people to avoid it, causing serious injuries and death. Unexpectedly, the examiner did not wait for Liu Linsheng to finish his statement and immediately forbade him from speaking, announcing that the driver involved in the accident would be released and not sent to court for investigation or compensation. This situation clearly shows that the concession authorities were protecting the British Public Bus Company, and the deceased died with a grievance that could not be cleared. Knowing that I am weak, I can only ask the association to help redress the grievance so that the driver can be warned and will not become more negligent, which will encourage the evil consequences of disregarding human life and ensure the safety of citizens in the future, etc. Based on this, after a detailed investigation by our association, regarding the case of Liu Ansheng, although the driver of public bus number 253 on Route 5 did not commit the crime of intentional homicide, at the time, he was speeding recklessly, taking the wrong route, driving too fast, and did not honk the horn to warn people to avoid it, which was negligence causing death, and he violated Article 291, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law, which states that a person engaged in business who causes death due to negligence in business is undoubtedly guilty. The concession authorities, because the Public Bus Company is a British company, protected it, and released the driver involved in the accident without sending him to court to be punished as he should have been, which is illegal. The Public Works Department should uphold the spirit of impartiality and selflessness and send the driver involved in the accident to court for punishment, otherwise, it would violate the wishes of all taxpayers and encourage the driver's negligence and disregard for human life, and the Public Works Department would be an indirect accomplice to murder. Your committee is the mouthpiece of the taxpayers and the protector of the rights of citizens, so we request that you negotiate with the Public Works Department to achieve the purpose of punishing the crime in the Liu Ansheng case. Furthermore, your committee's contribution to the Public Works Department, ordering the Public Bus Company to install protective iron bars on public buses, has not yet been adopted by the Public Works Department, which is incomprehensible. This simple measure cannot be accepted by the taxpayers, which is absurd. Furthermore, our association has something else to say. The speed of public buses should also have a corresponding limit, otherwise, it would be detrimental to the safety of citizens, which is obvious. For public bus drivers who cause incidents in the future, they should be sent to court for punishment, and the opinions of citizens should be humbly accepted, and there should be no unnecessary protection so that the safety of citizens can be guaranteed and avoid unexpected disputes. We hope that your committee will forward this, and we will be grateful. (Note: The Taxpayers' Association has sent a letter to the Public Works Department for investigation.)

Tragic Fire at the Republic Road Intersection

Another Body Found Yesterday

The Huili Clock Shop at the intersection of Republic Road in Zhabei recently had a fire, resulting in the tragic deaths of five people and the injury of one person, as reported in various newspapers. At the time, four bodies were recovered, which were examined by Prosecutor Lei of the Shanghai District Court. There was still one body missing because the arsonist was at large and his whereabouts were unknown. The shop had fire insurance of 13,000 taels, guaranteed by four insurance companies. It was necessary to wait for all four guarantee companies to arrive before the search could be carried out. It was not until yesterday afternoon at 3 PM that the burnt body of Weng Cuiyu was found by people sent by the insurance companies. It was already charred. Due to the hot weather in recent days, the body had decomposed and a stench was spreading. After being retrieved, it was placed at the front door of the shop. Passersby all avoided it. Landlord Lu Abao reported to the Shanghai District Court yesterday, but the prosecutor was out on official business, so he will have to report to the court again this morning to request an examination.

Senior Bookseller Chen Xie Gong Passes Away

Mr. Chen Xie Gong, courtesy name Yin, served in the Wenming Book Company and the Guoxue Rotary Club during the Guangxu years. In 1912, he co-founded the Zhonghua Book Company with Mr. Lu Fei Bohong and others. He pioneered the compilation and printing of textbooks suitable for the Republic of China, becoming a pioneer in China's cultural undertakings. He served as the general store manager, director, printing factory director, and director of the company, serving in the book industry for more than thirty years. He was always admired by his colleagues. This spring, his mother passed away, and Mr. Chen was deeply grieved and felt unwell. He initially felt abdominal pain and went to the hospital for diagnosis, where he was diagnosed with pleurisy. He followed his doctor's advice and stayed in the hospital for rest. After more than two months, he seemed to recover slightly. Unexpectedly, on the 18th of this month, his condition suddenly changed to pneumonia, and he passed away on the morning of the 19th at his residence in Shanghai, at the age of 53. He is survived by six sons and two daughters. The funeral will be held tomorrow (the 26th) morning, and his remains will be temporarily placed at the Xijin Guild Hall. A memorial service will be held on September 2nd at the Qingliang Temple Zen Monastery in the Xinjia Garden on Xinzha Road, following his wishes not to send out obituaries. Mr. Chen was pure and simple in his character and courageous in his work. His sudden death was mourned by all his colleagues at the company.

Recent News on the Construction of Xinhua Village

Xinhua Village, built by Xinhua Bank on West Tiyuhui Road, has sold two-thirds of its properties in less than two weeks since it was presented to the public, demonstrating the bank's excellent management and the superior location, which has won the trust of the public. It is recently heard that because houses are being built in the summer, the cement sets faster, and the project is easier to solidify, which is better than other times, so they are not afraid of the summer heat, and work is supervised day and night in this climate of more than 100 degrees Fahrenheit. The project is progressing rapidly, and the materials used are especially excellent. It is estimated that there are four types of houses that are about to be completed, and there are three types of houses under construction: A, C, and special. There are fourteen houses that are in the process of applying for permits and being built. The shops, vegetable markets, etc. managed by the bank have been completed and are being arranged and decorated to facilitate the purchase of residents. The affiliated primary school building is also being planned and built. Overall, the current situation of Xinhua Village can be said to be not far from the completion of the entire new village plan. As for the addition of police posts and the relocation of bus stops, it is reported that active negotiations are underway. The bank has consistently worked hard on the construction of the new village and continued to progress until it is completed, and its service spirit is admirable. On Sunday of last week, there were more than 30 people who went to visit and negotiate about the remaining one-third of the land, which shows the public's concern and interest in Xinhua Village.

Reef Discovered in Langya Bay

Hydrographic Office Issues Notice to Seafarers

A reef has been discovered in Langya Bay (Gaosha Port) on the south coast of Hainan Island. Its position is at 303 degrees north from the top of West Brothers Island (height 340), a distance of 3.03 nautical miles, approximately 109 degrees 40 minutes east longitude and 18 degrees 12 minutes north latitude. The reef is submerged at low tide. The Hydrographic Office of the Navy Department has issued a notice to alert seafarers to this hazard as the reef lies on a major navigation route.

Page 14

Rickshaw Pullers' Deflation Riot

Mastermind Defendant Interrogated Yesterday

Sentencing Scheduled for the 30th of This Month

The case of the rickshaw deflation riot mastermind defendant, prosecuted by the police, was heard again yesterday afternoon at 2 PM in the first criminal court by Judge Zhan Liangce of the First Special Court. First, the police lawyer Ru Bao Yi stated that he was prepared to present the so-called important witness from last time and requested that the public be prohibited from attending. The court granted the request, and after the audience left, the court began questioning the witness (whose name and testimony are not disclosed due to the police's request, fearing accidents), which lasted for more than half an hour. Then, the defendants were questioned. According to the defendants Zheng Fazhu, Zhu Fengxiang, Cang Gongwen, and He Wushan, the purpose of the petition was because they saw reports that the chairman of the Rickshaw Affairs Committee, Massey, was about to resign, and that the Rickshaw Affairs Committee had accepted the rickshaw owners' eight conditions, so they petitioned to retain Massey and not change the new regulations. Lawyer Ru then stated that it had been found that the defendants Zhu Fengxiang and He Wushan had not pulled rickshaws for six or seven years, so it was inappropriate for them to represent rickshaw pullers. Then, Chinese Detectives Nos. 94 and 162 presented evidence to investigate the circumstances of Zhu and He not being rickshaw pullers, but Zhu claimed that he was indeed a rickshaw puller, and the numbers of the rickshaws he pulled were 8808 and 8813, and the owner was Yin Zhiling. He Wushan claimed that he had switched to selling vegetables for a period of time but resumed his rickshaw pulling life after the situation stabilized, and the owner was someone on Tiantong Road. Lawyer Ru for the police then stated that the defendant Zheng Fazhu had collected a so-called handling fee of 120 yuan on behalf of the new rickshaw owners Shi Haiyuan and Wang Zaocheng when collecting new licenses from the Rickshaw Affairs Committee, so he was additionally prosecuted for fraud and obtaining property under Article 363 of the Criminal Law. The court then summoned Shi and Wang to the court. The testimony of the two was roughly the same as the points mentioned by Lawyer Ru in yesterday's newspaper. (Omitted) At that time, because the defendant Zheng Fazhu denied that Shi and Wang had been to his house, the court inquired about the location of Zheng's residence, which took a long time and caused many disputes. However, Wang Zaocheng heavily attacked Zhu Maocheng, a member of the Rickshaw Affairs Committee, during his testimony, saying that the 120 yuan handling fee was actually obtained by Zhu and that Zheng was just Zhu's puppet. However, Zheng completely denied it. The lawyers on both sides argued fiercely over issues such as the time of payment. The questioning of the witnesses ended at 5 PM. Chen Tingrui, the lawyer representing the Rickshaw Owners Association, then stated that the total amount of civil losses was 37,154 yuan, including 990 damaged vehicles. There was a detailed list and requested that the sentence be pronounced at the same time as the conviction. If the court considered the calculation to be complicated, it requested that it be transferred to the civil court for trial. The court, seeing that the facts were clear, ordered the debate to begin. Lawyer Ru for the police and the lawyers Wu Linkun, Yao Yongli, Fu Ganghou, Yu Chengxiu, and Zhang Yifan for the defendants Zheng Fazhu, Zhu Fengxiang, Cang Gongwen, He Wushan, and Zhu Shuqiao debated each other until 7 PM before the debate was concluded. Judge Zhan then announced that the verdict would be announced at 9 AM on the 30th of this month.

Yesterday's City God Procession

Yesterday was the traditional Ghost Festival. The City God of this county, along with his four attendant deities, paraded to distribute alms to the lonely spirits who lacked offerings. In the morning, all the heads of the various associations gathered. At noon, the procession set out, circling through the inner and outer city. Later, they reached the altar outside Xiaoximen to distribute alms and burn a large quantity of silver ingots and silk. After a short rest, at 6:30 PM, the "Night Gathering" (俗稱夜會) set off from the altar, again circling through various parts of the southern city, turning into Dadongmen and the northern half of the city before returning to the temple. The entire route was managed and kept in order by the heads of the various associations, and the order was quite good.

Route Petain

A Large-Scale Red Pill Manufacturing Operation Busted

The Mastermind is at Large, Only Workers and a Driver Arrested

Red Pills and Machinery Seized Valued at Tens of Thousands of Dollars

Jin Jiulin, the Superintendent of the Special Unit of the French Concession Police, received a tip from an informant a few days ago that a large red pill manufacturing operation had been set up on the third floor of number 310 Route Petain. It was said that they were manufacturing pills all night long to avoid the attention of neighbors. Based on the report, Superintendent Jin, along with Detective Zhang Ziying, Qian Yumin, Deputy Detective Zhou Bingcheng, Detective Liu Dianlong, Bu Zhenglong, and others, secretly went to the address to search it at 1:45 AM yesterday. Arriving at the location, they saw bright lights on the third floor. When they knocked on the door and entered, the workers upstairs had already noticed and quickly turned off the lights and pretended to be asleep. The detectives groped their way up to the third floor in the dark, turned on the lights, and found a large-scale operation. However, no one was there. The pill-making tools were in disarray, indicating that the workers had hidden themselves after hearing the noise. They searched the servants' quarters and found people sleeping, with the fire in the stove under the pill-drying box still burning brightly. They immediately arrested the manufacturing workers on the bed: Guan Xiaocai (43 years old, from Ningbo), Li Shifan (22 years old, from Guangdong), Chen Xiaokang (14 years old, from Haimen), Chen Xiaosheng (13 years old, from Haimen, Chen Xiaokang's younger brother), and the driver Zhang Xiaolin (22 years old, from Jiangbei). They then began the search and seized 130 bags of already made red pills, weighing 78 pounds, and one large package weighing 41 pounds, totaling 119 pounds in three large flour sacks and one large paper package, containing a total of 198,200 pills. They also seized three large drying ovens for manufacturing, three sets of pill-making boards, one rolling stick, four pounds of raw materials, fourteen pounds of white powder, four boxes of red dye, two table boards, one vat, two basins, three copper brushes, four long orange sticks, two pairs of pliers, one bundle of hemp rope, six pieces of plywood, four white porcelain basins, one iron box, one leather box, one glass funnel, seven sieves, one case of advertising paper (about hundreds of sheets), 250 red pill paper covers, ten sticks of sealing wax, one large balance scale, three large steelyards, six small steelyards, one stamp, and five knives. The value of all these items was estimated to be tens of thousands of dollars. They were loaded onto two trucks and taken to the police station. However, the mastermind boss was at large and had not been caught. Yesterday afternoon, the police station sent Guan and the other four to the Second Special District District Court. Judge Xiong Huiping presided over the preliminary hearing in the First Criminal Court. Gu Shouxi, the police station's lawyer, presented the details of the raid and the seizure of the items, as well as the arrest of the five defendants. He stated that the police station needed ten days to investigate further and arrest the mastermind boss, as they had not yet had time to conduct a thorough investigation or list a detailed inventory of the seized items. Guan Xiaocai confessed that he was an accomplice and that the boss of the illicit red pill manufacturing operation was Zhang Xiaoheng, who had fled upon seeing them being arrested. Li and the two Chen children also admitted to being accomplices in the manufacturing. Zhang Xiaolin confessed to being a driver. The court reviewed the confessions and adjourned the hearing to September 3rd. The defendants were remanded in custody.

Record of the Half-Yearly Meeting of the Child Welfare Association

Kong Xiangxi Reports on Past Work and Future Hopes

Pan Gongzhan Delivers a Speech Hoping for the Popularization of Child Welfare Work Nationwide

The Chinese Child Welfare Association held its half-yearly meeting for this year yesterday at 5:00 PM in the auditorium on the fifth floor of the National Christian Young Men's Association on Museum Road. President Kong Xiangxi reported on past work and future development plans. The details are recorded below:

(Meeting Order) The order of the meeting was: (1) Chairman of the meeting: Vice President Luo Yunyan, (2) Opening remarks by President Kong, (3) Financial report by accountant Lin Kanghou, (4) Work report by General Secretary Xu Jianping, (5) Speech by Pan Gongzhan, (6) Temporary proposals from members, (7) Guidance from representatives of party and government organizations, (8) Refreshments, (9) Adjournment.

(Representatives Present) Representatives present included President Kong Xiangxi (represented by Luo Yunyan), Director of the Municipal Education Bureau Pan Gongzhan, President of Shanghai University Liu Zhanen, General Secretary of the World's Chinese Student Association Zhu Shaoping, Wu Zhijian and Gao Mingqiang of the Chinese Leprosy Relief Association, Secretary-General of the Bankers' Association Lin Kanghou, Director of the Municipal Health Bureau Li Tingan, Director of the Municipal Police Bureau Wen Hongen, and over two hundred others.

(President Kong's Speech) After the meeting began, President Kong Xiangxi (represented by Luo) delivered a speech, saying, "Gentlemen, today our association is holding its sixth annual half-yearly meeting. So many comrades and guests have come to participate, which shows the interest and enthusiasm of all of you for child welfare work. This truly makes me feel very happy and fills me with infinite hope for the future of child welfare work and the Child Welfare Association. In the first half of this year, we have already established child welfare branches in Beiping and Luanxian. Starting in the second half of this year, we will add another branch, which is the Nanjing Child Welfare Association. Now, people in Shanghai, as well as people all over the country, are showing great interest and enthusiasm for child welfare work. Just based on this, we can confidently believe that the success of China's child welfare work is absolutely not a problem, it is only a matter of time. Today, we are holding this half-yearly meeting here to conduct a thorough review of the past and to make a far-reaching vision for the future. We must base ourselves on the existing foundation of the past and attempt to achieve greater development and greater success in the future. Perhaps we have inevitably had many mistakes and failures in the past, but we can use the experiences of past mistakes and failures to correct our own observations, to supplement our own plans, and to strengthen our own efforts, step by step towards the road to success. I think you all still remember that when we held the fifth annual meeting in January of this year, we passed a so-called 'Five-Year Work Plan of the Chinese Child Welfare Association' (with a total of sixty points), which aroused considerable attention and considerable praise from the general public. However, a plan written on paper is certainly not enough, we should work hard to gradually realize it. Therefore, after the closing of the annual meeting, we considered the limited capacity of our association and the urgent needs of society and formulated our first year of implementation, including the following aspects: In terms of general affairs, (1) convene a national conference of child welfare leaders, (2) establish child welfare branches in various places, (3) expand the Children's Day commemoration movement, (4) provide materials needed for the Children's Year, (5) strengthen domestic and foreign liaison and publicity, (6) strengthen the cooperation and collaboration of related groups, (7) raise funds, and (8) request the allocation of base to protect the base. In terms of protection, (1) promote children's laws, (2) promote children's courts, (3) conduct district surveys of child labor, (4) stop the sale of children, (5) report child abuse, and (6) rescue special children. In terms of relief, (1) establish reformatories to help homeless children, (2) establish complaints offices to rescue forced prostitutes, (3) expand the Tangshan Road Child Welfare Training Home, (4) expand the Yangshupu Child Welfare Nursery, (5) plan to establish Child Welfare Nurseries in Pudong or Zhabei. In terms of health, (1) establish the Zhabei Child Welfare Experimental Zone, first setting up a Child Welfare Clinic, (2) establish the Jiangwan Child Welfare Tuberculosis Sanatorium, (3) pilot the Nanjing Children's Health Park, (4) hold children's health movements, and (5) publish various books on pregnancy, infant care, and other health topics. In terms of education, (1) hold child welfare lectures and broadcasts, (2) promote the Modern Parents Monthly, (3) promote children's savings, (4) hold exhibitions of children's toys and reading materials, (5) add to the Parents Education Series, and (6) publish new era parents and children education puzzles. In total, there are thirty tasks to be carried out in this year, the 23rd year of the Republic of China. From January of this year to now, almost seven months have passed. In these seven months, we have already carried out some of the tasks, some are in progress, and some are to be carried out in the second half of the year. At the time of holding this half-yearly meeting today, we are willing to report our work situation to the society most faithfully and ask for social criticism and guidance. The achievements of the association's work in the past half-year will be reported by the General Secretary, so I don’t need to say more about this. What I want to say now is that I hope that you will truly and without any politeness examine our work and add a review. There was a merchant who often said to his customers, 'If you are not satisfied with our service, please honestly and frankly tell us so that we can correct it. If you are satisfied with our service, please do your duty to promote it to your friends so that we can expand the scope of our service in the future.' Today I can say the same thing: 'If you are not satisfied with the work of the Child Welfare Association, please honestly and frankly tell us so that we can correct it. If you are satisfied with our work, please do your duty to promote it to your friends so that we can expand the scope of our work in the future.' In the past, the association has been able to achieve a little success entirely because of the constant supervision and support of sympathetic people in society. As the Chairman of the Association, I should represent the Association and express my sincere thanks to all sympathetic people. From now on, the association's responsibilities will be heavier and the association's work will be more, so our needs for society will certainly be more urgent than in the past. Therefore, while thanking you on the one hand, on the other hand, I have to represent the association and ask you to give us more severe supervision and more extensive support. Now, the most noticeable country in the world is Soviet Russia. In the past, no country in the world looked up to Soviet Russia, and they all thought that Soviet Russia was a culturally backward country. However, since the success of the Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan, all countries in the world have looked at it with new eyes, acknowledging that Soviet Russia is also a civilized country and also a powerful country. Speaking of our China, if we stand from the standpoint of child welfare, we are indeed inferior to others in every way. Usually, when foreigners talk about China, they always think that China is a culturally backward country, which does not pay attention to all aspects, especially the happiness and education of children, and has never known how to pay attention to it. I hope, and firmly believe, that if the Five-Year Plan of the Chinese Child Welfare Association can be realized item by item, then the happiness and education of Chinese children will be able to develop greatly, and China's international cultural status will certainly be able to improve, and we will no longer hear people say that our China is a culturally backward country. All of this depends on our efforts and our hard work. I am willing to encourage everyone together."

(Work Report) Then, General Secretary Xu Jianping reported on the general situation of the work, saying, (A) General Affairs Group (1) Hold fundraising campaigns, (2) Hold child welfare dance parties and theater parties, (3) Prepare for the Nanjing Child Welfare Association, (4) Promote Children's Year, (5) Promote Children's Day, (6) Convene a national conference of child welfare leaders, (7) Take over the Zhabei Civilian Training Home, (B) Protection Group, (1) Handle children's cases, (2) Request the right of representation for child welfare organizations, (C) Relief Group, (1) Child Welfare Training Home, (2) Child Welfare Nursery, (3) Subsidize child welfare organizations, (D) Health Group, (1) Establish a Child Welfare Clinic, (2) Prepare to build a Child Welfare Sanatorium, (E) Education Group, (1) Publish the Modern Parents Monthly, (2) Publish Parents Education Posters, (3) Publish Parents Education (4) Ask the Ministry of Education to issue a general order requiring secondary and higher schools to pay attention to parents education, (5) Hold child welfare broadcasts and lectures. Then, Lin Kanghou reported on the economic situation.

(Director Pan's Speech) After the report, Director Pan Gongzhan of the Municipal Education Bureau gave a speech, saying that the organization of the Child Welfare Association dates back to the 17th year of the Republic of China. It has been six or seven years since then. Thanks to the enthusiastic and responsible guidance of the members, a foundation has been laid so far. All the constructions for the preservation and care of children have been roughly scaled, and the results are remarkable. According to its purpose, it is originally the meaning of the ancient sages of our country to educate the young and care for the elderly, such as Mencius said, "Respect the elderly in my family, and extend it to the elderly in other families; love the young in my family, and extend it to the young in other families." It is nothing more than feeling that the strength of the country and the peace of society all depend on the people to protect the orphans and old and young people in the society. This kind of cause should have been promoted by the country. Now, in the midst of internal and external troubles, the people spontaneously organize groups to assist the government in adopting and caring for children who have lost their parents. It is indeed a rare move. In the future, I hope that comrades who are enthusiastic about child welfare in China and abroad will make further efforts to promote it so that its scope will be extended to the whole country, then the orphans and weak women of the whole country will be very fortunate. Then the meeting was adjourned.

The Yifei Case Continued Yesterday

Hong Chengde and His Concubine Still Did Not Appear

Yifei's Mother Wept Bitterly in Court

The famous courtesan Yifei, originally named Chen Zhujun, and Yang Qiusun's grandson Binghu, a compradore of Puyi Real Estate Company, died together in the bathroom of Hong Chengde's residence in the Sun Apartments. Now Chen's mother, Chen Wangshi, claims that her daughter was killed by Xie Peide, the sales director of Shanghai Cement Company, Hong Chengde, and Hong's concubine. She has hired lawyer Ye Fikang to file a private prosecution against Xie and others, requesting that they be punished according to law and that Xie be ordered to return her daughter's jewelry. The First Special District District Court has already conducted a preliminary hearing. Due to the need to investigate witnesses, the hearing was postponed. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Zehan opened the court again to continue the hearing. The defendant Hong Chengde and his beloved concubine still did not appear, and the essential witness Yang Qiusun also failed to appear. According to the plaintiff Chen Wangshi, she heard that Hong's wife and concubine (are now in Shanghai). She requested that an arrest warrant be issued. She claimed, "My daughter was indeed beaten to death by the defendants. If it was suicide, it would be difficult to shoot herself twice. Now, two people were beaten to death, not two dogs. Moreover, I only have this one daughter. Who will I rely on from now on? I beg the old master to redress my grievance, otherwise, my grievance will never be cleared. My daughter came to 2 Baker Road on April 26 and told me that Xie would put her to death. If she died unfortunately, I had to redress her grievance. At that time, I did not believe it and comforted her. Unexpectedly, my daughter was taken away that day after returning home. If my daughter wanted to commit suicide, why would she commit suicide in the Sun Apartments?" She cried bitterly as she spoke, and the audience (were mostly moved to tears). At this time, the plaintiff's lawyer expressed dissatisfaction with the investigation report made by West Detective Hua Desheng of the Jing'an Temple Police Station regarding the case. He said that the case occurred on April 28, but the report was made on the 17th of this month, and its content was quite similar to Xie's defense. For example, the testimony of Hua Detective He Yunpu, which was unfavorable to Xie, and the fact that Chen Zhujun's jewelry was taken away by Xie after her death, were generally omitted, which could not satisfy the plaintiff. The court then summoned West Detective Hua Desheng for questioning. The detective first stated the situation of investigating the bodies in Hong's bathroom with Hua Detective after the incident. He then said that he saw a jewelry box on the table in the living room, and the detective (checked the situation of the items) only claimed that he asked the people present who owned the jewelry, and Hong Chengde replied that it was his. Since the box was not related to the incident, he did not take it to the police station. As for the details provided by He Yunpu in the previous court hearing, I only heard about them for the first time that day because He did not report the situation to me as he said. The court then summoned He Yunpu for questioning. According to his testimony, after I finished investigating the case that day and returned to the police station, I reported the situation to Detective Hua. As for the jewelry, after I checked it that day, I did not have time to ask about it because I had to go to the hospital to transport the two bodies to the autopsy site. It was not until the autopsy the next day that I asked Hong Chengde about the whereabouts of the jewelry, and Hong said that Xie Peide had taken it away. West Detective Hua Desheng continued to state that today's (case report) was copied from the records and investigation case books in the police station, and the books were recorded after the investigation at that time. At this time, the witness Xu Hongjun slowly came from outside. Xu worked as a gatekeeper at the Sun Apartments. The court stated that according to He Yunpu's previous testimony, he had asked Xu about it on the day of the incident. Xu told him that when Chen Zhujun arrived at the Sun Apartments by car on April 26, there were five or six men and women in the car. Later, Chen tried to escape, but was stopped by Hong's maid, and someone was also watching her in the room. Therefore, he immediately ordered Xu to enter the witness stand and asked whether the above situation was true. However, Xu's answer was rather ambiguous. The court questioned him again and then said that he also heard it from passers-by and Hong's maid when they were chatting. The court then ordered his concubine to appear in court for questioning at the next hearing, and the plaintiff then requested that the essential witness Yang Qiusun must also appear in court and must not evade again. Judge Wu then adjourned the hearing for a continued hearing.

Wang Zhaocheng, Involved in the Liu Chongwu Case, is Sentenced

Sentenced to One Year and Six Months in Prison

Maotai Yang Goods Store at 310 Xinzha Road and Yuheng Yang Goods Store at 339 Hankou Road were warned by the Iron-Blooded Elimination of Traitors Group for selling inferior goods between November 18th and 24th of last year. Because they ignored the warnings, the manager Wang Zhentao and his partner Wang Yirong were shot with a handgun, resulting in fatal injuries. Later, the police station arrested the criminals Liu Chongwu, Pan Hongsheng, Cao Songtao, Tian Shuiyang, and others and sent them to the First Special District Court. As a result, Cao was sentenced to twelve years in prison, Liu to seven years, and Pan and Tian were each sentenced to six years. They confessed that the handguns and bombs belonged to Wang Zhaocheng, a member and adjutant of the Shanghai Civilian Righteous Army Expedition to the Northeast, who was from Haining. On June 15th of this year, Hua Detectives Ma Bingzhang and Wang Guangtian of the Jiaxing Road Police Station arrested him and sent him to the First Criminal Court. After the interrogation was over, he waited for the sentence. Yesterday morning, Judge Liu Yugui presided over the trial and sentenced Wang Zhaocheng to one year and six months in prison for joint murder. The number of days of detention before the trial was determined to be two days for one day of imprisonment. The other parts were not guilty. The defendant's agent lawyer declared an appeal, and the court approved it.

Three Suicide Attempts

Fortunately, All Survived

Yu Shengfa Yu Shengfa, a native of Ningbo, is 22 years old and works at Zhongji Silk Store at 10 Baoan Lane, Tianjin Road. Yesterday, he was fired by the manager of the store due to an accident. After Yu heard the announcement of his dismissal, he felt as if struck by lightning and was in despair. At around 7:30 PM, he secretly swallowed raw opium in an attempt to commit suicide. After being discovered, the police station was notified and the central ambulance was dispatched to the scene, and he was rushed to Renji Hospital for treatment.

Gu Zhu Shi Gu Zhu Shi, a local young woman, is 27 years old and rents a residence at 127 Gaochang Temple, Nanshi. Her husband, Gu Yinsheng, is a customs broker. Recently, due to poor business, he has been heavily in debt, and creditors often come to the door to collect debts. As a result, there are frequent quarrels between the couple. Yesterday morning, another creditor came to demand payment. Unable to avoid it, she decided to commit suicide and secretly swallowed a gold ring. Later, she was discovered and taken to the hospital for treatment.

Qin Zhou Shi Qin Zhou Shi, a woman from Dantu, is 25 years old and lives at 89 Guangqi Road, Nanshi. Her husband's name is Jia Hui, and he works as a salesman in a soap factory. He likes to indulge in pleasure and often does not return home for several days, neglecting all the expenses of the family. Yesterday morning, Zhou tried to ask her husband for household expenses, but he beat her instead. Afterwards, she was so angry that she secretly swallowed opium and attempted suicide. Later, neighbors called the police, and she was taken to the hospital for treatment.

Deep Affection of Japanese Women

Preferring to Die with Their Chinese Husbands

Ito Tetsuko, Wife of Pan Xiangxi

Yonezawa Yukiko, Wife of Zhang Yaosheng

According to yesterday's Japanese-language Shanghai Daily, Pan Xiangxi from Wenzhou, along with his wife Ito Tetsuko (from Hanaoka Town, Akita County, Akita Prefecture, Japan) and their two children, returned to China from Japan. They were stopped by the police of the Japanese Consulate at the wharf and were not allowed to go to Wenzhou. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. After they were placed under the surveillance of the Japanese police at the Hinode Ryokan in Yifeng Lane, Kunshan Road, they were originally ordered to go to the Consulate General the next day to listen to the order. Unexpectedly, at 10:30 PM on the 22nd, they secretly left the hotel. At 11:20 PM, the hotel telegraphed the police station of the Consulate General. According to the Tokyo Hochi Shimbun, Zhang Yaosheng, a worker at the Senju Standard Shoe Store in Adachi Ward, Tokyo, was forced to return to China on the 20th due to labor permit regulations. Since Zhang's wife, Yonezawa Yukiko (a Japanese woman), married Zhang, their love has been deep and unwavering. Yukiko's mother (Zhang's Japanese mother-in-law, 61 years old) also treats Zhang very kindly, regardless of national boundaries. This time, when she heard that the Japanese government had deported Zhang, she suddenly came to Tokyo with her daughter from Osaka, saying that Yukiko had already given birth to two children, "Even if I want to put her to death, I don't want to live apart from Zhang. No matter what, I must go to China with Zhang." Now Yukiko and others have set off to Dalian to cross over to China.

After Xu Qingyun's Death

Eldest Daughter Sues to Divide Inheritance

Mediation Fails

The late Xu Qingyun, also known as A Mao, a local tycoon in foreign goods in the French Concession, owned several stores solely and jointly during his lifetime. He resided at 58 Avenue Hoche in the French Concession, a self-owned property. He first married a Ms. Chen, with whom he had a daughter named Xu Daxin, now thirty-three years old and still unmarried. Twenty years ago, Xu also took another Ms. Chen as a concubine. After they moved in together, she bore him a son and two daughters. The love between husband and concubine was deep, and he treated his first wife, Ms. Chen, like worn-out shoes, not even caring about her livelihood. Therefore, three years ago, Xu's wife, Ms. Chen, hired lawyer Li Xinyang to sue Xu at the French Concession Court. The result was that both parties settled the case with 25,000 yuan. In the years of 1931 and 1933, Xu Qingyun and his first wife passed away one after another. All the inheritance, estimated to be over a million gold, was controlled by Xu's concubine, Ms. Chen. Recently, Xu's eldest daughter, Xu Daxin, requested to divide her late father's inheritance, but her stepmother, Ms. Chen, ignored her. Therefore, Xu Daxin hired lawyer Zhang Shizhao as her agent and filed a petition with the mediation court of the Second Special District Court, requesting mediation for the division of the inheritance. The court, based on the petition, summoned both parties yesterday. Judge Tu Shenjie opened the court for mediation. The petitioner's agent, lawyer Zhang Shizhao, was represented by Peng Jianxun. The opposing party, Xu Chen, hired lawyer Xue Dubi, who was represented by lawyer Cao Shoulin. First, the petitioner's lawyer Peng stated that the late Xu Qingyun had a total inheritance of over a million, now estimated at 800,000. The petitioner should receive one-fourth, totaling 200,000 yuan. He requested the court to instruct the opposing party to distribute the inheritance accordingly. The opposing party's agent, lawyer Cao, stated that the petitioner's mother had previously been involved in a lawsuit with Xu Qingyun. Both parties reached a settlement through a mediator, and a written agreement was made as proof. Since there was already a settlement, how could there be another request? He urged both parties to settle the matter amicably. The opposing party's lawyer also stated that the opposing party was willing to settle with a thousand yuan. The petitioner's agent lawyer stated that the amount of the petitioner's claim was very large, and the amount offered by the opposing party was vastly different, making it difficult to reach a settlement. Judge Tu, seeing that mediation was unsuccessful, declared the mediation to be unsuccessful and ordered that a separate lawsuit be filed.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Cables the Ministry of Finance

Instructing the Release of Shaoxing Wine with Transportation Permits

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday telegraphed the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, stating: "To the esteemed Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, on the 23rd of this month, we received a letter from the Shaoxing Wine Trade Association, stating that a member of the association, the Nanchezhan Xingongji Shaoxing Wine Transportation Company, reported that the company had 100 jars of Lao Dongming sample wine, declared by Xieheyong to be shipped to Dalian, and 200 jars of Bei Dongming Jingda Shaoxing wine, declared by Shenyu to be shipped to Beiping. On the morning of the 18th of this month at 9:00 AM, they first used three flatbed cars to transport 68 jars of Jingda wine and 100 jars of sample wine for transfer, with staff from both Xieheyong and Shenyu customs brokers carrying transit customs documents and origin-based provincial transportation permits accompanying the cars. Unexpectedly, when the wine cars reached Hujunying Road, inspector Wang Bingxia of the Shanghai Inspection Office and others, believing that they had not affixed Jiangsu Province tax stamps, considered it tax evasion. After being informed that the aforementioned Shaoxing wine was for export, and that the tax stamps had been affixed at the place of origin in Zhejiang Province, and that according to regulations, no additional stamps were required when passing through Jiangsu Province, and presenting the customs documents and transportation permits for verification and detailed explanation, inspector Wang and others disregarded everything, sounded the alarm, and ordered the wine and cars to be sent to the Second District Police Station, and three car drivers were also detained at the same time, resulting in significant business losses for the company. Please investigate and handle the matter,' the letter stated. After discussion at the sixth executive and supervisory emergency meeting of our association, it was determined that since the export procedures for the aforementioned Shaoxing wine had been verified and there were no violations, yet it was forcibly detained, it was clearly infringing on business. It is appropriate to submit a request for a swift telegram instructing its release to alleviate business difficulties, which would be beneficial," the letter stated. Article 14 of the Regulations on Fixed-Amount Tax for Local Wine stipulates that local wine produced in other provinces that passes through this province should, upon entry and exit, present the transportation permit or voucher from the producing province for verification by the local tax collection authority. If the verification is consistent, the tax collection authority should affix its seal, along with the date, and stamp it as verified for entry or exit, and release it immediately without delay or extortion. Therefore, according to regulations, no tax is required when passing through a province. The Shaoxing wine in question came from Zhejiang Province and possessed a transportation permit from the place of origin for provincial departure, as well as transit customs documents, accompanying the cars. According to regulations, there were no violations. Since Jiangsu Province was a transit province, there was legally no reason to pay taxes or affix stamps. The inspection office detained the wine without authorization under the pretext of not affixing Jiangsu Province tax stamps. Is this due to a lack of clear regulations, or is it intentional obstruction? It is appropriate to report the situation and request your ministry to investigate and order the release immediately, for the sake of public convenience. Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce respectfully submits the request."

Dispute over Manure Transportation in the Southern District of Shanghai

City Farmers' Association Requests Thorough Investigation

Since the Shanghai Southern District Farmers' Association was accused by some manure transportation cart owners of extortion and corruption, a dispute has arisen, attracting social attention. The City Farmers' Association, considering the matter to be related to the livelihoods of farmers and the reputation of the association, has decided to conduct a thorough investigation to determine the truth. The supervisory committee of the City Party Headquarters has reviewed the accounts of the district farmers' association over the years. Hundreds of cart owners, yesterday, jointly submitted a petition to the City Party Headquarters, the Social Affairs Bureau, the City Farmers' Association, the Central Military Police Political Training Department, and other agencies, denying the accusations and presenting the facts of the matter to seek public opinion. The original petition is excerpted below: "Petition regarding the Shanghai Southern District Farmers' Association acting as agent for the collection of sanitation fees, and denying the listed accusations, requesting review. The manure tax in the Shanghai Southern District began in the late Qing Dynasty. At that time, even under the despotic rule of the imperial system, farmers repeatedly staged strikes and protests against the manure tax due to their vital interests. Despite being imprisoned, they did not yield and eventually achieved the goal of tax exemption. After the establishment of the Republic of China, some people again proposed the manure tax, but it was not implemented. Later, Yuan Shikai seized power, and harsh taxes were continuously levied. The manure tax, which impoverished the poor farmers, was again contracted to merchants. Over the course of ten years, the tax rate increased repeatedly. Each manure cart paid four yuan per month, one yuan per year for the copper plate fee, and six jiao to one yuan for each festival fee, in addition to other demands. Moreover, due to the contractors selling the manure to other locations, there was often a shortage of fertilizer for agriculture, causing farmers great suffering. Under the oppression of warlords, there was no way to appeal. In 1927, the Party Army conquered Shanghai. Under the guidance of our Party, the farmers in the Shanghai Southern District organized the Farmers' Association to alleviate their suffering. After repeated struggles and hardships, they managed to reduce the tax rate and reached an agreement with the Sanitation Department to have the Farmers' Association act as agent for the sanitation fees for agricultural manure transportation carts, with the principle that farmers transport and use the manure themselves and are not allowed to sell it. After a resolution by our association, in addition to the fixed tax rate of two yuan and one jiao and nine fen per manure cart per month, an additional voluntary donation of eight jiao and one fen was collected, and a fee of two yuan was paid each summer to fund the association's activities, such as running schools, subsidizing self-defense, promoting cooperation, and providing tea and medicine. The Farmers' Association had no funds of its own and relied on this fee due to the frequent addition of matters related to sanitation, increased expenses for work attendance, and staff salaries. This was taken from the public and used for the public, and it was voluntary for the farmers. For several years, although the Farmers' Association has changed several times, the fees have remained the same, because the tax rate is lower than before and the procedures are more convenient, so everyone is happy to comply. Moreover, various taxes have increased in recent years. Even merchants who contract sanitation fees from the Finance Bureau have increased the tax rate annually. Only our manure transportation carts in the Shanghai Southern District, which are about to unite, have not increased taxes and have remained the same for several years. However, this time, a small number of cart owners from other provinces (also members of the Farmers' Association) violated the principle of self-transport and self-use, sold fertilizer, violated the agreement, and conspired to establish a fertilizer sales company, hoping to monopolize the market, enrich themselves, and ignore the agricultural fertilizer in the Shanghai Southern District. The Farmers' Association, because these people were destroying public interests, intended to punish them according to the association's rules. These people, seeing that their plan could not succeed, harbored resentment and initially accused the Farmers' Association of defrauding money in court, but the case was dismissed. Now, they are accusing them in military agencies. On the 19th of this month, the Farmers' Association convened a meeting of manure cart owners to discuss disposal methods, and they led military police to arrest the Farmers' Association staff. The case has now been transferred to the City Executive Committee for processing. Yesterday, we read a news report entitled 'Shanghai Southern District Manure Cart Owners Request Strict Punishment of the Farmers' Association,' which stated that all 204 manure cart owners in the Shanghai Southern District jointly petitioned the Political Training Department of the Central Military Police Regiment, requesting strict punishment because the Farmers' Association was holding the association's affairs, seizing power, and exploiting them. We were shocked to read it. Not only are the accusations completely fabricated, but we farmers have never been listed as accusers. The false accusations should be thoroughly investigated by your association (department) (bureau) to maintain the manure transportation, so that the agitators cannot use their cunning tricks. Otherwise, the right to self-transport and self-use fertilizer, which we have fought for for several years, will be sacrificed by these people, and the past suffering will reappear today. We are terrified at the thought. We farmers cultivate and eat here, and rely on fertilizer as an essential element for agriculture. Several people jointly operate a manure cart and take turns to collect manure. These hundreds of manure carts actually supply fertilizer to thousands of farming households. Now, they are suddenly being destroyed. For the sake of our vital interests, we respectfully present the facts and request a clear understanding. It is also necessary to state the accusations and requests. (1) In the accusation document, it states 'The presenters (102 Shanghai natives and 102 from other provinces) all earn a living by pulling carts and dumping manure in Shanghai.' This clearly indicates that they make a living by selling manure, which has violated the principle of self-transport and self-use. They deliberately included the names of hundreds of us farmers, dragging things out in the hope of overturning the established case and collecting taxes to enrich themselves. Their intentions are obvious. (2) 'For each new cart, the City Finance Bureau instructs the Public Utilities Bureau to issue a white porcelain license plate, charging seven yuan and two jiao, but they demand 25 yuan to 35 yuan for each plate.' We farmers have not been defrauded of this money, and it is clearly fabricated out of thin air. (3) 'Request to make the accounts public.' This has been handled by the City Executive Committee, and whether there are any irregularities will be revealed. (4) 'Return the soft paper licenses for manure carts.' This is stored in the association for proof of membership when receiving licenses. If these people request the return of the soft licenses, it means they are leaving the Farmers' Association and can freely sell manure, achieving their ambitions. (5) 'Request to allow 204 people to withdraw from the Farmers' Association.' We farmers have always regarded the Farmers' Association as a group of farmers. Only through unity can we alleviate suffering. These people are destroying the group and should be expelled from membership to eliminate the harmful elements. In short, we farmers will not allow a minority to destroy the group and vow to fight together with the indomitable spirit of the past few years. Respectfully submitted to the Executive and Supervisory Committee of the Shanghai City Party Headquarters, the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, the Political Training Department of the Second Regiment of the Central Military Police, the Shanghai Municipal Farmers' Association, and manure cart owners of the Shanghai Southern District Farmers' Association (139 people), represented by Ma Yisheng, Zhang Zhongjie, Cao Jinhua, Zhao Yundi, He Shanxin, Chen Mingzhao, Mao Zixiang, Shen Changgen, Zhu Xinlian, Zhang Linquan, Shen Wensheng, Shen Lanqing, Zhou Qisheng, Yao Jinqing, etc."

Three Fires in One Day

Weihaiwei Road: At the western end of Weihaiwei Road and Tongfu Road, there were more than ten old-style bungalows in Youzheng Lane. At 1:20 PM yesterday, Liu Rongcai, a tenant in the loft of Chen Yushan's house at No. 13, was burning paper ingots at home to worship ancestors yesterday as it was the fifteenth day of the seventh lunar month, which caused a fire. It quickly spread out of control. Although the fire brigade immediately dispatched vehicles to rescue, it was difficult to water due to the narrow lane. As a result, a total of seven rooms at Nos. 10, 11, 12, 13, 14, 15, and 16 were burned to ashes. The Shixingzhiji silk weaving factory on the opposite side also had one of its rear buildings burned down, but the losses were minimal. When the fire was raging, Zhang Yulin (49 years old), a resident of No. 10, jumped from the loft and injured his waist. He was then taken to Renji Hospital for treatment by ambulance.

Daxi Road: At around 11:00 AM yesterday, a fire broke out in a straw shed at No. 311, Daxi Road, Xuhui, due to careless cooking. It quickly spread out of control. The fire brigade was alerted and dispatched vehicles to the scene to put out the fire. Only one straw house was burned down. However, when the fire was raging, a woman escaped from the fire and was severely burned. She was taken to Guangci Hospital for treatment by ambulance. It is said that her injuries were serious and her life may be in danger.

North Shaanxi Road: At around 11:00 AM yesterday, a fire suddenly broke out at the Qingxiangzhai tofu shop at No. 122, North Shaanxi Road. Thick smoke filled the air and the fire was very fierce. The fire brigade was alerted and dispatched vehicles to the scene and made every effort to put out the fire. Only one floor was burned down.

Severely Poisoned, Life in Danger

Chen Bowen, a Cantonese woman and dancer at the Yixiafei Dance Hall on Avenue Masnan and Avenue Joffre in the French Concession, is 30 years old, graceful, and fond of dressing up. She is one of the most beautiful dancers in the hall. Recently, she felt economic pressure and suddenly had suicidal thoughts. The waiter discovered her and quickly reported to the front desk, who reported to the Old Gate Police Station and ordered patrolman No. 303 to come. He also summoned the manager of the dance hall and took her to Renji Hospital for treatment by car. However, she was severely poisoned and was already unconscious when she arrived at the hospital. Although the doctor gave her injections and medication, her life was still in danger at midnight.

Xue Xianggen Sentenced for Arson

Sentenced to Seven Years in Prison

The Xie Feng Woolen Store at No. 156, Hubei Road, has been open for only a few months and had fire insurance of 10,000 yuan with the Ning Shao Company. Because the business was sluggish and losses were heavy, the store owner, Xue Xianggen from Wuxi, had bad intentions. On the night of the 9th of this month at 12:30 AM, he poured kerosene on the furniture and set it on fire, intending to claim compensation. After the Central Fire Brigade received the report, it immediately dispatched fire trucks to put out the fire. Later, Old Gate Police Station detectives Chong Ruiqing and He Renrui found out the truth and arrested him. Police lawyer Gan Jingxian filed a public prosecution with the First Special District Court in accordance with Article 187, paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law. The trial has been concluded. Yesterday morning, Presiding Judge Feng Shide announced the verdict: Xue Xianggen was sentenced to seven years in prison for setting fire to a dwelling currently in use. The number of days of detention before the judgment is confirmed shall be deducted from the sentence at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment.

Questions and Answers for Readers

Re-discussing the Chicken-or-Egg Problem

——Answering Hu Jie and Others

A few days ago, we published an article on the "chicken or egg" problem, which attracted a lot of attention from readers. However, that article focused on the biological aspects of the explanation, and the content was somewhat too specialized, so some readers could not fully understand it. Now, we will use a more accessible way to explain this issue.

On the surface, this question seems to only concern chickens, but in reality, it is not limited to chickens. There are similar situations and similar questions in everyday life. For example, we go to the store or factory to work in the morning and return home to eat and sleep in the evening. We use our labor to earn a little money each month and bring it home to support our family. At the same time, our family uses the money I provide to prepare the necessary clothing, food, housing, and other things for my life. If my family did not have my support, they could not live. But if I did not have my family to take care of the necessities of life, my life would also be problematic, because I have to spend all day working and really do not have the time to take care of my own life. Therefore, we have to ask: "Am I supporting my family, or is my family supporting me?" Isn't that a bit similar to the question we asked: "Did the chicken come first, or the egg?" Or some people will say: There are many people in society who don't have a home; they live a vagrant life, working during the day, and having no fixed place to live or eat at night. They spend one night here, one night there, one meal here, and one meal there. They don't have a home, but they can still survive, right? Yes, there are such people, but for these people, there are other similar questions that arise. When these people are hungry, they have to use the money they earn from work to buy food at the shop. When they want to sleep, they have to use the money they earn from work to buy a place to sleep at a temporary lodging. They have to rely on the strength of the food vendors and the owners of the lodgings to sustain their lives. At the same time, the food vendors and the owners of the lodgings have to rely on the diners and lodgers to support their own lives. So we have to ask again: Are the diners and lodgers supporting the owners, or are the owners supporting the diners and lodgers? Isn't this the same kind of question? (To be continued)
