Educational News

Ministry of Education Inspector

Recently Inspects Vocational Education in Hunan, Provides Improvement Suggestions

The Ministry of Education recently sent Inspector Gu Zhaolin to inspect the state of vocational education in Hunan Province. The results of the inspection have been reported to the Ministry of Education. The key points of the report regarding the urgent need to improve vocational education in Hunan are summarized below:

(A) General Issues

(1) The vocational schools established by the province often have overlapping departments. For example, the Provincial Advanced Technical School has a mechanical engineering department, and the Provincial Changsha No. 1 Vocational School, Hengyang No. 3 Vocational School, and Baoqing No. 4 Vocational School also have metalworking departments. Although the names are different, the content is largely the same. The dyeing and weaving and applied chemistry departments also have the same situation. The following measures should be taken to correct this: A. Separate management of departments. This measure involves extracting the part of a department's categories that is suitable for the local situation, increasing the amount of research and learning, and reducing the scope of the original curriculum to achieve specialization in art. For example, in western Hunan, where there is abundant production of oil and leather, the applied chemistry department of Changde No. 2 Vocational School can specialize in oil painting or leather making. In the Baoqing area, there are many fibrous raw materials available for papermaking. The bleached paper researched and improved by Baoqing No. 4 Vocational School is better than local products and can specialize in papermaking. If the above method cannot be applied within a department, and the establishment of the department cannot be changed for the time being, the same departments in two or more schools can be merged into one school to change to a single-department setting. B. Centralized management. If it is possible to thoroughly transform vocational schools throughout the province, it is best to centralize management. Suppose Changsha No. 1 Vocational School runs a metalworking department, then the metalworking departments of Hengyang and Baoqing should be merged into Changsha. If Changde sets up an applied chemistry department for oil painting, leather making, etc., then the two applied chemistry departments of Hengyang and Baoqing should be merged into Changde. If Baoqing specializes in dyeing and weaving, then Changsha, Hengyang, and Changde should be merged into Baoqing (in terms of geography, it would be more convenient for Changde to handle dyeing and weaving and Baoqing to handle applied chemistry). In this way, factory equipment can be easily planned from an overall perspective, and it is easy to allocate teaching talents appropriately. However, there are difficulties in the process of transformation, and careful planning and proper implementation should be made.

(2) The operation of vocational schools in Hunan Province shows that private schools have achieved quite good results. For example, Xiuye Chuyi, Gongyu, and other schools can select one or two subjects in vocational disciplines to refine students' skills, so that they can engage in production after graduation, which is commendable. Provincial schools should also pay attention to this in the future to avoid being superficial.

(3) Among the schools with mechanical engineering departments, only the Provincial Advanced Technical School and the private Chuyi School have better factory equipment and can undertake the task of manufacturing mechanical components. If the design of various machines is more difficult, they can imitate the imported small-scale soap-making, oil-making, and printing machines that are commonly used to promote new local industries. Other schools with metalworking departments with poorer factory equipment should immediately respond to local production conditions, pay attention to repairs, equip various parts, and manufacture new agricultural tools, hardware miscellaneous parts, and other work for practical use.

(4) The ceramic products of the Provincial Guiyang No. 5 Vocational School are still considerable, but the school site is remote and transportation is inconvenient. The school relocation plan proposed by the Department of Education is indeed a crucial plan and should be implemented. The Provincial Zhijiang No. 6 Vocational School originally had three departments: oil painting, applied chemistry, and agriculture. Due to simple equipment, it is quite difficult to operate. One or two departments should be discontinued in accordance with the principle of single-department establishment, so as to concentrate efforts and focus on rectification.

(5) Changsha Private Hengcui and Autonomous Minfan, such as girls' vocational schools, either concurrently run embroidery and sewing departments or specialize in sewing departments, and the results are considerable. Other similar schools with better results should be convened to contact each other and establish a product research association to seek improvement. It can be handled according to the following principles: A. In terms of embroidery, in addition to the original landscape, flower, and bird screens and couplets, and patterned tablecloths and cushions that are commonly seen by Chinese people, new European and American patterns and foreign social habits and consumer habits should be studied to prepare for sales overseas. These items must be beautiful and practical. In addition, major European and American projects, contemporary scientists from various countries, portraits of celebrities, and other famous works of art from ancient and modern times can also be widely collected to enrich teaching materials and produce high-quality products with artistic value. B. In terms of sewing, it is generally practical. The cooperative formed by students and graduates of various schools offers clothing at lower prices, but exquisite Western-style clothing and uniforms are inferior to those sold in stores. Women's accessories have not yet been taken into account. It is best to divide them into exquisite and regular types according to social needs. The price of exquisite products can be appropriately increased, which can not only meet the needs of high-end consumers in society, but also improve students' work skills. C. The product research association should hold exhibitions for observation and facilitate sales.

(6) The principals of provincial vocational schools and the teachers in charge of vocational departments have too few opportunities to contact the industrial and commercial sectors outside the province. The Department of Education should send them to factories and vocational schools in Shanghai and Guangzhou in rotation for planned visits and inspections to learn from them. There must be at least two people for each common subject. It can be held in stages by year depending on the financial situation, but the visiting personnel must have the obligation to report the gains from the visit to other provincial schools with the same department.

(7) Vocational education in Hunan Province lacks an organization for research and promotion. If the funds are limited and the previously established vocational education committee cannot be restored, the Department of Education can convene enthusiastic people from the education community and specialized technical personnel to form a consulting and design group to promote it.

(8) If the provincial vocational schools are to be reorganized according to their original situation, the initial step should be to complete the relocation plan for the Advanced Agricultural School, the continued construction plan for the Advanced Technical School, the addition of factory equipment for Baoqing No. 4 Vocational School, and the relocation of school buildings for Guiyang No. 5 Vocational School, which are the most urgent and should be allocated funds as soon as possible.

Minister of Education Wang Shijie Proposes

Establishing Two Industrial and Agricultural Schools

Opening Fee of One Million Yuan

Has Been Approved by the Boxer Indemnity Fund

(Nanjing, 24th) Minister of Education Wang Shijie believes that since 1924, universities have been established everywhere, but there is no one that focuses on vocational training that can serve as a national model. This has resulted in a lack of technicians, foremen, ordinary engineers, and farm technicians that society needs. No one is responsible for the practical work of proofing, supervising, and arranging farms, which is a major defect in China's education. To remedy this, he requested that the British Boxer Indemnity Agency allocate funds in succession to centrally run two schools in suitable locations, one of an engineering nature, focusing on machinery, civil engineering, electrical engineering, and applied chemistry, and one of an agronomic nature, focusing on rural agriculture, horticulture, sericulture, etc. The opening fee for the two schools is estimated at one million yuan, which has been approved. The Ministry of Education is currently negotiating with the Boxer Indemnity to allocate funds.

Pan Gongzhan and Liu Zhanen

Opinions on Reforming the Education System

Many people in the educational circles of Peking and Tianjin, such as Jiang Menglin and Hu Shi, believe that the existing education system is not perfect. They have jointly submitted a request to the Ministry of Education to modify the education system. The original text has been published in various newspapers. This reporter visited Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, and Liu Zhanen, President of Shanghai University, to inquire about their opinions. They told us the following:

Pan Gongzhan's View: Mr. Pan greatly agrees with the principle of the proposal to modify the existing education system proposed by Hu Shi, Jiang Menglin, and others in the educational circles of Peking and Tianjin. He believes that the existing education system does have areas that urgently need to be reformed.

Liu Zhanen's Opinion: Mr. Liu strongly agrees with the reform of the education system and believes that the system should be unified. The implementation of a system is the responsibility of the whole country. If the whole country can implement the same system, the effect will be great. Mr. Liu also believes that the implementation of a system must be tested. Only after testing can we know the merits and demerits of the system. Mr. Liu also believes that there are too many flaws in the existing education system and that a good education system is needed. Mr. Liu believes that the proposal of Hu Shi and others is of great value and has submitted his opinions to the Ministry of Education.

Representatives of Various Institutions Urge the Payment of Arrears

(Nanjing, 24th) Representatives of various institutions in Peking and Tianjin came to Nanjing to urge the payment of arrears. A solution has been agreed upon by all parties: (1) The Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Finance will jointly submit a report to the Executive Yuan, and when the national treasury is sufficient, all arrears will be repaid. (2) The salaries of teachers and staff who have not left the school will be gradually repaid. (3) Those who have left the school will be repaid immediately. The representatives, believing that their goal has been achieved, are scheduled to return to Peking on the 25th to report their mission.

Brothers Ye Yanhua

Will Go to Nanjing Today to Petition

Before Leaving Japan, They Were Warned by the Japanese Not to Expand Publicity

After Arriving in Shanghai, Their Words and Actions Were Greatly Restrained, and They Did Not Dare to Reveal Their Grievances

Ye Muhua, a overseas Chinese in Japan, was brutally murdered in Japan. His brothers, Ye Yanhua and Ye Lunshi, in order to appeal to the motherland, report the truth of Muhua's brutal murder, and receive education in the motherland, specially arrived in Shanghai on the Nagasaki Maru the day before yesterday. Because the Ye brothers were severely threatened by a certain party before leaving Japan, they were very cautious in their actions after arriving in Shanghai. It is learned that the Ye brothers have planned to take the train to Nanjing today to report to the government. The reporter of Shenshi News Agency specially inquired about the details as follows:

Actions Greatly Restrained The Ye brothers returned to China together to appeal to all parties and arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday. For the sake of convenience, the Foreign Affairs Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau sent personnel to the pier to take care of them. After arriving in Shanghai, the Ye brothers went to temporarily stay at the home of a relative on Caishi Road in the French Concession. Their words and actions were greatly restrained. When people from all sides went to visit, the Ye brothers declined to see them all, because there was some unspeakable pain. According to inquiries by the reporter of Shenshi News Agency, when the Ye brothers departed from Nagasaki, they were severely threatened and warned by a certain police authority, stating that they were not allowed to expand publicity in the country after returning to China, otherwise the property and lives of their families would not be protected, etc. After they returned to Shanghai, they felt that they were being monitored, so although they returned to the country with a belly full of anger, the pain of killing their brother and the shame of the nation could not be expressed to the compatriots in the country. The depth of their inner pain can be imagined.

Will Go to Nanjing Today to Petition The Ye brothers have decided to take the train to Nanjing this morning to pay their respects to the authorities to report and request something. Yanhua also plans to find a school in Nanjing to enroll in and receive education in the motherland. Muhua and his brothers were all born in Japan and were influenced by the education there. They can hardly understand a word of the national language, but their heart of longing for the motherland has become more and more urgent under the influence of what they have seen and heard in Japan. Before Muhua was brutally murdered, the brothers had discussed with their parents and prepared to return to the country to study. They first moved from Kumamoto to the Overseas Chinese Elementary School in Nagasaki to make up for Chinese language. It was during this period that the tragedy occurred. Yanhua's mental stimulation was even deeper, so he decided to return to the country to study and no longer planned to return to Japan.

Private Prosecution Demands Compensation The criminal part of the Muhua murder case has been decided by the Japanese court under an unfair trial. The civil part has been filed in civil private prosecution with the court by Muhua's father, Ye Xiuyi, demanding compensation of 16,000 yuan. However, judging from the fact that the Japanese side is punishing the murderers, it is expected that it will be difficult to obtain satisfactory results. It is heard that Muhua's eldest brother, Lunshi, will still return to Japan after Yanhua's study is arranged to take care of the family affairs in Japan, and will decide to return to the country with his family within a short period of time.

Municipal Bureau of Education Orders All Schools Not to

Withhold Transfer Certificates on Pretexts

And Should Use the Transfer Certificates Made by the Bureau

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education issued an order to all secondary schools, stating, "Students have the freedom to choose schools and transfer schools within the scope permitted by law. According to Article 72 of the Middle School Regulations, 'Middle school students who pass the examination at the end of the semester or academic year may request the school to issue a transfer certificate if they must transfer to another school or if there is a situation stipulated in Article 62.' Article 62 states, 'Students who have no semester grade in a subject or whose grades are failing in more than three subjects, or only two subjects have no semester grade or are failing, but the subjects are any two of the four subjects of Chinese, English, Mathematics, and Labor in junior high school, or any two of the subjects of Chinese, English, Mathematics, and Physics in senior high school, should be demoted to the school in the lower semester. If there is no corresponding grade in this school, a transfer certificate may be issued.' Therefore, within the scope of the above regulations, students may request the school to issue a transfer certificate for transfer. However, it has been found that various secondary schools in this city often fail to comply with the above regulations and withhold transfer certificates on pretexts, which is inappropriate. Furthermore, all schools should use the transfer certificates made by this bureau when issuing transfer certificates and must not use other documents as substitutes for transfer. An order has been issued, but a few schools have still failed to comply effectively, which is also wrong. All of the above situations are expected to be corrected by each school if there are any, and if not, they should work harder. Schools must not create difficulties for students transferring schools on pretexts, so as not to interfere with the merit order. An urgent order to comply with this order."

In order to unify the uniforms of students in public and private secondary and elementary schools in the city, the Municipal Bureau of Education has formulated uniform measures in accordance with the Ministry of Education's Regulations on Student Uniforms, taking into account the local conditions in the city. Once a reply is received, it can be decided, announced, and implemented.

Rural Old Customs

The Qingmiao Society is About to Rise Again

Welcoming Gods and Feasting Reaches the Pinnacle of Superstition

The County Agricultural Education Center Actively Carries Out Reforms

Every year during the new autumn season in the countryside, there is a practice of the Qingmiao Society, where gods are welcomed with feasts to pray for a bountiful harvest. Each village forms a group, and the villagers prepare wine and dishes, gathering with relatives and friends to connect and strengthen their bonds. The average cost per household is more than ten yuan. In these times of rural destitution, it is necessary to eliminate this practice. However, due to long-standing habits, it is difficult to reform it immediately. The 15th Rural Improvement Conference of the Zhuanqiao Farmer Education Center resolved to utilize the Qingmiao Society to showcase agricultural products and exempt them from taxes. The trial will start in the Kangjiazhai basic education area on the 29th of this month. Farmers will bring out their agricultural products, gather them for display, and allow people to observe, compare the quality of the products, and provide rewards. This way, it will truly match the name and purpose of the Qingmiao Society. No idols will be set up in the society. In addition to lectures, a storyteller will be invited to sing stories of loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame, in order to reform bad habits and save money.

Shanghai's

Children's Health Camp (4)

— Zhou Shang

Family Contact: There were a total of 59 children, with a roughly equal number of boys and girls. Most of their families were in business, followed by academia, and then the medical field. The press and legal professions also accounted for a considerable number. The families were mostly middle-class or above. This is something we should pay attention to. In the first few days of the camp, some parents came to visit every day. This seemed inappropriate because it was easy to bring infectious germs into the camp, which would harm the overall situation. Secondly, when children saw their parents, siblings, they would inevitably feel reluctant to part and develop "homesickness." Although there were many children in the camp and life was comfortable, "leaving home for a mile is not as good as staying at home." This is "a universal feeling, a common sentiment." Therefore, the camp formulated visitation rules, setting Mondays, Wednesdays, Fridays, and Sundays as visitation days. The visitation restrictions in foreign summer camps are very strict. Since China's national conditions are different and this is the first time we are doing this, it's okay to relax a little. When children entered the camp, they often brought a lot of money, books, and snacks. This was detrimental to the camp rules and harmful to their health. Therefore, everything was collected and returned to their families separately, explaining the advantages and disadvantages. Fruits and fruit juices were returned and used at designated times in the rest area. However, it is always best not to bring them to the camp because the camp provides appropriate food and drink, so there is no need to bring your own. The camp asked the children to write letters to persuade their parents about these issues, which was not only very interesting but also very effective. In the fifth week, a family day was held, and people from all walks of life were invited to watch performances of daily life. The personality, physical and mental shortcomings, and character of each child were reported to the parents in detail so that they could find ways to correct them and continue the orderly and good life of the camp after they left. The toothbrushes used by the children were not suitable, and the toothpaste could not be used because of the strong mint flavor. Therefore, the Family Industry Society, Children's Dental Hospital, physicians Gu Hailing and Su Jielang came to the camp to distribute toothbrushes, toothpaste, and mouthwash, and trained the children in brushing methods. They also gave each parent a booklet on oral hygiene to promote it. Food is a very important thing. Fearing that some parents were not clear about it, the camp asked the Yamei Company to donate the book "Children's Nutrition" by Su Zofei and send it to the parents so that they could follow it. Dr. Fei Kunnian was also invited to give a lecture on "Bathing" to correct past mistakes. Health education penetrates into the family. In the future, children will teach adults, and their progress can be guaranteed.

Financial Report: After Mr. Pan Gongzhan became the director of the Education Bureau and Mr. Li Tingan became the director of the Health Bureau of Shanghai, a "Central Plan for Health Education" was published. Last year, we wanted to run a summer camp for children with tuberculosis in Gaoqiao, but due to various difficulties, our courage was suppressed, and it eventually became a bubble. This spring, the two bureaus sent me to Japan to study health education. Seeing their rapid progress, I couldn't help but sigh three times. After returning to China, I immediately engaged in the establishment of this camp. Coincidentally, Zhang Wei and Zhang Junjun of the Chinese Association for the Prevention of Tuberculosis, the Children's Welfare Association, and the Children's Morning News also had the intention of running such a business. Therefore, our five institutions jointly managed it. Each institution contributed 200 gold, totaling 1,000 yuan, and each sent a portion of its staff to work in the camp. As a result, the 1,000 yuan was still insufficient. In addition to the 15 yuan per child, totaling over 800 yuan, there was still a shortage of about 400 gold. The use of funds is now reported as follows: (1) Subsidies for the teaching director and teachers found outside: 200 yuan. (2) Wages: 100 yuan. (3) Travel expenses: 150 yuan. (4) Food expenses: 400 yuan. (5) Nutritious products (milk, tofu, pulp, etc.): 200 yuan. (6) Fruits: 120 yuan. (7) Fuel: 50 yuan. (8) Laundry: 120 yuan. (9) Haircuts: 14 yuan. (10) Water and electricity: 150 yuan. (11) Stationery: 50 yuan. (12) Teaching materials: 50 yuan. (13) Equipment (toys, phonographs, etc.): 200 yuan. (14) Miscellaneous expenses: 150 yuan. (15) Posters and advertisements: 50 yuan, totaling 2,004 yuan. This is the estimated amount for the fourth week. At least 20 yuan was subsidized for each child. The newspaper advertisements were donated by major pharmacies and bookstores such as Zhongxi, Jicheng, and Zhongfa. Some of the equipment, such as the radio, small animals, and baseball, were borrowed by the author himself. The milk was also discounted by Liyuan Dairy Farm. The people in charge, doctors, and nurses all volunteered. Lu Zaiming's kitchen also volunteered half the time. Otherwise, several hundred yuan would have been spent without seeing anything. This is the help from society that we should thank. (The End)

Ministry of Education Orders Pingjin

Bian E Xiang Bao Ji Wan

Improve Physical Education in Primary and Secondary Schools

Hao Gengsheng, a physical education supervisor of the Ministry of Education, inspected the physical education facilities of primary and secondary schools in Beiping, Tianjin, Kaifeng, Wuchang, Changsha, Baoding, Jinan, Anqing, and other places when he inspected the physical education of colleges and universities in the above-mentioned places. In Beiping, he inspected 68 middle schools and 12 primary schools. In Tianjin, he inspected 19 middle schools and 7 primary schools. In Kaifeng, he inspected 24 middle schools and 11 primary schools. In Wuchang, he inspected 9 middle schools and 8 primary schools. In Changsha, he inspected 26 middle schools. In Baoding, he inspected 5 middle schools. In Jinan, he inspected 7 middle schools. In Anqing, he inspected 12 middle schools. In total, he inspected 170 middle schools and 38 primary schools. He has recently reported the points that should be commonly improved in the physical education of primary and secondary schools in the above-mentioned places to the Ministry of Education. On the 23rd, the Ministry of Education issued an order to the education departments of the above-mentioned provinces and cities, instructing them to order the schools to pay attention to the improvement. The original order said, "According to the report submitted by Hao Gengsheng, the supervisor of the Ministry of Education, on the inspection of physical education in primary and secondary schools in Beiping, Tianjin, Kaifeng, Wuchang, Changsha, Baoding, Jinan, Anqing, etc., after investigation, all the points mentioned are appropriate. In addition to separate orders, the original report is now urgently excerpted and instructed separately as follows:

(1) Most schools often hold morning exercises and recess exercises to improve the health of students' minds and bodies and to cultivate students' habits of loving sports. The intention is good, but generally physical education teachers stick to the old methods and do not change. The teaching materials they use are too old, which leads to students perfunctorily following the routine and not benefiting in any way. The Ministry should issue an order to the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities, instructing the primary and secondary schools under their jurisdiction to adopt new German-style natural exercise teaching materials for morning exercises and recess exercises. (The newly compiled "Detailed Items for Physical Education Teaching in Primary and Secondary Schools" by the Ministry has this teaching material for reference) to improve the situation.

(2) Most schools' physical education teachers often hold other positions or teach other subjects, rather than being full-time physical education teachers. If their duties are not specialized, their spirit will inevitably be scattered. It is already impossible to expect them to settle down and work hard. How can we expect them to work hard to improve and systematically develop physical education? In view of this situation, the Ministry should order all schools to hire full-time physical education teachers in the future and not allow them to teach or hold positions in other schools.

(3) Recently, secondary schools have often neglected students' daily life problems, such as food and lodging. Dormitory rules are extremely lax, and food and drink management is entrusted to students, which leads to a group of young students being unruly and unrestrained, without any restraint. They sleep at irregular hours, eat irregular amounts, and even shout and make noise, doing everything. This not only affects the school's discipline but also hinders the health of students' bodies. From now on, all schools should be strictly ordered to pay attention to the students' food and lodging problems so that students can have a stable life. They should comply with this order and report it.

Spring and Autumn

Peking Duck

— Yongcai

After reading the description of Empress Dowager Cixi and ducks in "Records of Imperial Fragrance," I thought of Peking ducks. Peking ducks, anyone who has been to Peking has probably tasted this unique roasted duck.

Peking ducks and roasted ducks from other places can be said to be fundamentally different. (1) Special Duck Raising Method: All the duck feed is carefully selected. Every meal is to feed the duck until it is full, because they are afraid that the duck will lose weight if it exercises too much. They are not allowed to swim in the water and are kept in the garden all day long. (2) Roasting Method: Although it is the same as other places, the fuel is different. The fuel for roasting ducks is not ordinary firewood, but jujube tree branches. It is said that this is also a reason for the deliciousness of Peking ducks. (3) Eating Method: In the south, roasted duck is always a side dish. Although it is sometimes used as a main dish, it can be said that it is very rare. Peking duck is not like this. There are at least ten restaurants in Peking that specialize in roasted duck. After sitting down in the restaurant, the waiters will bring a few raw ducks for you to choose from. After a while, they will bring the freshly selected duck roasted and show it to you whole. Then two waiters will stand outside the door, one cutting and the other plating, sending the meat and skin up in basins. The way to eat it is to roll the duck meat and skin in thin pancakes made of flour, commonly known as lotus leaf pancakes, smear them with some sauce, and eat them together. The duck bones and duck head are usually not served, but a large pot of soup is cooked with some Tianjin cabbage. If you are still not full after eating, you can ask them to stir-fry a large plate of noodles with duck oil. (4) The price is not expensive either. A duck that is enough for three people to eat, combined with other food, will not cost more than three yuan no matter what. This is also the main reason why Peking ducks are popular.

Speaking of Peking ducks, everyone will think of Yuhuattai outside the Qianmen Gate of Peking. It is said that this shop has been around for fifty or sixty years and specializes in roasted ducks. Business is still booming today.

Melon Talk

— Wang Shouqiu

It is popularly said that watermelon seeds come from the West, hence the name watermelon. This saying is not credible. If we follow this, then winter melon (also written as winter melon), pumpkin, and northern melon will all come from the East, South, and North, respectively? Watermelons are mostly round, but the melons in Dezhou are long. Because their shape resembles a pillow, they are called "pillow melons." Their taste is incomparably sweet. In recent years, melon vendors in the capital have planted this variety, so there are many pillow melons in the capital. However, their taste is much inferior to that of real Dezhou pillow melons, which is due to the soil quality. This year, the Nanjing Business Office of the Jinpu Railway is handling Dezhou pillow melons on behalf of them. The cost per load, including freight, is only four yuan and sixty-five cents. The locals in the capital can all enjoy a delicious meal.

Muskmelon is a fine product among melons. It is extremely small, like a honeydew melon, and its taste is extremely fresh. Unfortunately, it is not available in large quantities, which is quite regrettable for melon lovers! It is said that there are many melons planted in the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum in the capital, including Sānbái, pillow, and muskmelons. However, the production is not large, and it is not easy to buy them unless you are a person with important qualifications.

Sānbái melons have white skin, white flesh, and white seeds, hence the name Sānbái. They are also a fine product among melons. It is said that those produced in Suzhou are the best. Not only is the flesh of the watermelon edible, but also the skin and seeds are edible. The outer skin of the melon can be peeled off, cut into thin strips, pickled with salt, and mixed with sesame sauce and oil. It has a unique flavor and is a wonderful accompaniment to porridge. The seeds are stir-fried with salt water, which is no different from those sold in the market.

This year, due to the lack of rain, the melons are mostly weak and small, and their sweetness is even less than in previous years. The melon growers are discouraged by this blow, because they rely on this season's business to make a living for the whole year.

Ice Cream

— Nailing

Ever since we knew how to use ice to make food, the name "ice cream" has become "popular without being promoted." No matter what poor and remote place it is, as long as there is an "ice cream" vendor there, everyone will know this westernized name. I think that among the "foreign words" translated from English, none is more popular and widespread than this "ice cream"! Because "ice cream" makes you feel cool all over when you eat it, this thing is sold everywhere in the summer, and there are many, many people who eat it. It is said that when "ice cream" first appeared, many people were afraid of it because people who were not used to eating it would have their teeth ache as if they had swallowed a ball of fire. However, after a while, everyone got used to eating it and it became an indispensable blessing in the summer.

I remember when I was in Guangzhou in previous years, I often gathered with two or three colleagues in the summer, collected a yuan or a few dimes, and made a phone call to Chengji in Henan (the most famous ice cream shop in Guangzhou). In a moment, a whole bucket of "ice cream" was delivered. Then everyone surrounded the bucket and used bowls instead of cups to gorge on the "ice cream." Thinking of this happy way of eating, I still find it very interesting! However, I heard that the writer Peng Jiahua, who died last year, became ill from eating too much "ice cream," and as a result, his intestines broke down and he died of fright! There are so many contradictions in the world. Delicious things cannot be eaten too much, and good things are not often encountered. It is indeed meaningless to be a human being!

Gaoyou Eggs

— Guanying

"Selling Gaoyou eggs!" Recently, I have often heard this clear and sharp shouting in the streets and alleys. Among them are women, children, young adults, and old women. They all carry a basket of white, fresh, and clean duck eggs in their hands, shouting along the street. Judging from their clothes and earthy appearance, they have undoubtedly just run out of the countryside. In recent years, the bankruptcy of the rural economy has made it impossible for them to live in peace. They have all brought this unique local product - duck eggs - from the cities to sell and make a living. This situation is pitiful enough.

Usually, Gaoyou eggs cannot be bought for less than ten or even eleven or twelve cents in shops and stalls. Now, you can buy them for seven or eight cents from them. This is of course due to their simplicity and innocence, not knowing how to deceive and raise prices. But in this time of falling prices for everything, how can they not lower the price to sell? In fact, seven or eight cents a piece is really worth eating. Cut open, the fresh, yellow, and oily color inside makes people love it, and the excellent taste is indeed incomparable to those produced elsewhere. On these summer evenings, taking a cool bath, it is a real treat to eat it with mung bean porridge.

Gaoyou is a county in northern Jiangsu, a city along the Grand Canal. West of the river is a vast expanse of Gaobao Lake, with fertile land. Most of the residents along the lake rely on duck raising for their livelihood, in groups of thousands. Because the supply of fish, shrimp, and other ingredients is sufficient and convenient, the eggs they produce are exceptionally plump and delicious. The most famous is a double-yolk egg, which is larger than ordinary eggs. The yolk inside has the size of two ordinary eggs, which is because two eggs are produced together. When the author was studying in Huaiyin in his early years, he passed through Gaoyou, and when the boat docked at the dock, many rural women came on board to sell them. I once tasted a double-yolk egg. The color was fresh and the taste was delicious, which was far better than usual, and it is still memorable to this day.

Modern Drinks

— Zui Zhang

These days are the days of modernization. Everything will only thrive if it is modern. Even the street ice drink stalls by the roadside in Shanghai have become modernized. They also sell shaved ice with fresh oranges, and a straw is inserted diagonally into the cup. For compatriots of the lower and middle classes, spending a small amount of money to enjoy modern drinks in a modern way to relieve the intense heat is, of course, a very affordable thing. Therefore, this kind of modernized street ice drink stall is often full of customers.

But when we try to investigate the raw materials of the fresh orange shaved ice at street ice drink stalls, we can't help but be shocked. The main raw material for fresh orange shaved ice is, of course, fresh orange juice. In a glass or porcelain container, there is a fire-yellow liquid filled to the brim, and several cut-open Florida oranges float on top of the liquid. Has the water been boiled? Is the fire-yellow color dyed with toxic dyes? That is unknown. But if you go and carefully observe those cut-open Florida oranges, you can immediately discover that, whether on the skin or inside, there are often patches of grayish-black spots. It turns out that the owners of the ice drink stalls, greedy for cheap prices, buy rotten goods from fruit shops, cut off the terribly rotten parts, and throw them on the surface of the water as a facade.

As for the straw used to suck the ice water, that's even more unspeakable. Originally, the reason for using a straw to drink soda or ice water was to avoid the spread of infectious diseases. Therefore, after a straw has been used, it should be discarded immediately. But the owners of the street ice drink stalls are surprisingly stingy. The straw used by customer A is often inserted into customer B's cup after a while. The straw is made of paper, and after being soaked several times, it is, of course, limp and shapeless. If customer A has an infectious disease, the germs will undoubtedly be transmitted to customer B.

In this extraordinarily hot weather, everyone naturally wants to enjoy some refreshing drinks. But for those whose economic means are not very sufficient, one could consider: boiling a pot of water, adding a little white sugar to it, buying a few cents' worth of crushed ice to chill it thoroughly, and wouldn't that also be refreshingly cool? Why must one put on airs and drink this nominally modern, but actually not, drink, swallowing the juice of rotten fruit and the germs of unknown infectious diseases together?

Hangzhou Zhiweiguan's Wonton

— (Gray Horse)

Anyone who goes to Hangzhou for leisure must look for a few snack restaurants on the lake. But upon entering, one invariably eats two famous Hangzhou dishes, such as sweet and sour bream, clear-braised river shrimp, stir-fried shrimp kernels... and so on.

Yes, the water in West Lake is so clear and lively, so lovely; therefore, it cannot help but evoke the thought of eating special products from the water.

However, "Zhiweiguan" is also a famous restaurant in Hangzhou, and its business is very good. Its wontons are very famous. If you run in and eat a bowl of delicious shrimp wontons and drink a bowl of Huadiao wine, it's more flavorful than eating a few dollars' worth of snacks.

Having visited West Lake once, it is a pity that many people have never even tasted the wontons of "Zhiweiguan".

(Editor's Note: The large wontons of Hongxing Restaurant in the Ta Jian Nong in Gong Xiang Branch Alley in Suzhou are even better than those of Zhiweiguan. Those who know the taste can speak of this.)

Wuxi's Crispy Eel and Jiangyin's Soft Eel

— Yangtze River

I have lived in Jiangyin for generations, so please let me talk about Jiangyin first.

Jiangyin is located on the Yangtze River. In the Former Qing Dynasty, it was the place where students from the eight counties north and south of the Yangtze River, including Wuxi, Changshu, Jingjiang, and Taixing, gathered to take the imperial examinations to become scholars. At that time, the noodles of Jiangyin's Xinjing Garden were highly praised by the students from the seven neighboring counties. And in the summer, the best side dish to go with the noodles was, of course, eel shreds! For example, if we now invite three or five friends to walk into a restaurant in Jiangyin (whether you are eating noodles or drinking alcohol), the dishes that fill the table, besides one or two plates of "shrimp fry," are all eel shreds. And if you don't have enough to eat, the waiter will keep adding them. This shows how good Jiangyin is at eating eel shreds.

But eel shreds can be divided into crispy eel and soft eel. Crispy eel seems to be a specialty of Wuxi. Although Jiangyin also has it occasionally, it is not as well-made as Wuxi, just right. Conversely, soft eel is a specialty of Jiangyin, and there is none in Wuxi restaurants at all.

Once, passing through Wuxi, a friend from Wuxi invited me to eat noodles. When a plate of crispy eel was served, the friend proudly introduced it, saying: "This is crispy eel, a specialty of Wuxi, and there is none in other places." I ate a few chopsticks. Although I felt it was crispy and delicious, I always felt it was not as flavorful as Jiangyin's soft eel. So I then said: "Yes, although there is no crispy eel in other places, our Jiangyin's soft eel is even more flavorful. If you have the chance, please come to our county to try it and compare it!" At that time, that friend did not respond, and his eyes fully revealed a kind of disbelief. He thought that Wuxi's crispy eel should be unparalleled.

Another time passing through Wuxi, that friend smiled and said to me: "Indeed, indeed, Jiangyin's soft eel is much more delicious than Wuxi's crispy eel, and its taste is truly profound!" That friend had read ancient books, so his speech was very elegant. Later, I learned that he had gone to Jiangyin with several friends and tasted the delicious soft eel. "Hearing is not as good as tasting." The previous contempt had turned into today's praise, which was not surprising.

I have digressed too much. Now let me talk about the methods of making crispy eel and soft eel.

(1) Preliminary preparation: The so-called preliminary preparation is the same for both crispy eel and soft eel. That is to say, take live and kicking eels, kill them, remove their intestines, wash away the dirty blood, and then put them into boiling water for about two or three minutes before捞ing them out. (Some people also put the whole live eel into boiling water and then捞it out to wash and debone it, but that is a bit too dirty.) After捞ing it out, you can use a sharp little knife to cut open the eel's backbone left and right, and the backbone will naturally be removed, leaving only pure meat. At this point, the preliminary preparation is complete.

(2) Method of making crispy eel: First, mix one-fifth of wine, one-fifth and five of sugar, two-fifths of soy sauce, and five-tenths of salt, plus three or five slices of old ginger to enhance the flavor. Then put the washed eel shreds in and soak them thoroughly for about twenty minutes (the longer the better, if time permits). After that, take them out and put them into a boiling oil pot immediately (lard is best, soybean oil is also acceptable).撈 it out when it is slightly withered but not yet deteriorated, and it is crispy eel. When eating, it is fragrant and crispy, and you can dip it in vinegar or sesame oil to eat, as you like.

(3) Method of making soft eel: To make soft eel, the eel shreds are first fried in an oil pot, which is exactly the opposite of the order of steps in making crispy eel. When making soft eel, the degree of cooking in the oil pot must not be to the point of withering. When the whole body is wrinkled and the core is also cooked through, you can definitely take it out. After taking it out, you can soak it in a seasoning similar to that used for crispy eel. It is best to use a copper pot to stew it over a low flame for half an hour, otherwise, soaking it for three to five hours will also work. When eating, there is juice, so you don't need to dip it in anything. Jiangyin people like to add some ginger shreds to eat.

The methods of making crispy eel and soft eel have been briefly described above. The focus of whether it is cooked well or not lies entirely in the combination of the ingredients and the duration of frying in oil! If the reader can fry it according to this method, they will not be fooled. As for whether it is done well or not, that is the specialty of the chefs in Wuxi and Jiangyin, and we will not be able to learn it easily.

Personally, I have always been an admirer of soft eel, and its taste is much more profound than that of crispy eel.

Continued Rise in Foreign Call Loans, Head Money Remains the Same

Shanghai Japanese Factories

Fine Yarn Losses, Coarse Yarn Profits

Japanese yarn factories in Shanghai are finding it increasingly difficult to calculate costs after the increase in cotton import tariffs. Based on recent cotton prices, the cost of producing Japanese yarn using American cotton for 21s/42s is comparable to the market price, with almost no losses. 32s and 40s require a loss of 10 to 15 yuan per bale, while 16s and 20s can generate a profit of 2 to 5 yuan.

Grain: Flour Futures Rise After Opening

Wheat Prices Show Little Improvement

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, various months initially showed a flat and then rising trend. The quoted price for foreign wheat in Chicago was around 2-3 corners, and Canadian wheat was slightly better by 1-2 corners. At the opening, the price for the current month was slightly lower by 1 fen, while the price for September remained unchanged. Starting from October, mainland buyers gradually absorbed the supply, as the prolonged drought and disappointing autumn harvest caused rice prices to rise uncontrollably due to high demand. Consequently, those involved were actively speculating, and the market followed this trend, returning to firm and higher prices. By the fourth session, prices had rebounded by about 2 fen compared to the previous day. When the market opened in the afternoon, mainland buyers continued to push forward from the previous session, and buyers from Yingkou and other regions also slightly increased their purchases. In addition, the market sentiment also improved, so the opening price showed a profit. For example, December and January had once again exceeded the 7-corner mark. Considering the fearsome nature of natural disasters, the future of the people's food supply may be heading towards panic. It is unknown whether the government authorities have taken precautionary measures. As a result, the current month was better by 3 fen and 7.5 li compared to the previous day, September rose by 5 fen and 2.5 li, October rose by 4 fen and 7.5 li, November rose by 5 fen and 2.5 li, December improved by 5 fen and 2.5 li, and January improved by 4 fen.

Oil Market: White Tung Oil's Rising Momentum Remains Strong

Recently, the price of white tung oil in the Hankou market has been rising steadily because the route to foreign merchants is particularly smooth. Last week, the price was still only 29 yuan and 7-8 corners per dan, but it quickly rose sharply to 30 yuan and 8 corners. Then, it rebounded slightly to 30 yuan and 2 corners, but in an instant, it rose again to 30 yuan and 7-8 corners. Yesterday, it was still selling for 31 yuan and 1 corner and 5 fen. Last night's news added up to 31 yuan and 4 corners and 5 fen. The momentum is still strong. Based on the current situation, it seems that there is a possibility of further rises. Recalling the situation of the previous rising trend, whenever it reached above 30 yuan, it reached a peak. Foreign merchants would stop buying. Sources would gather, and various factors would come together to curb the rising trend and create a rebound. Therefore, every time it rises above 30 yuan, the eyes of the crowd will inevitably change. It is still not certain whether this time it can break out of the previous routine, open up a new face, and create a new record. Therefore, although the market trend is strong, people cannot help but have some concerns. Zhejiang is experiencing a prolonged drought, and the river water in the upper reaches of the Zhijiang River is extremely dry. Therefore, shipping is difficult. Hangzhou merchants have run out of stock, and it is unknown when the source will be smooth. It is heard that the current market requires 29 yuan per dan delivered to Shanghai, and not many can be handled. The stock of local trading houses has also been exhausted, and the remaining stock is scarce. Fortunately, sales are also scattered, so it is not enough to be stretched.

It began distributing the egg paper on the 20th, and in three days, a total of 540,000 sheets of autumn eggs were distributed, which is estimated to produce more than 100,000 dan of cocoons.

They can only ship silk to Shanghai for temporary mortgage loans to maintain operations. In recent days, a total of about 200 pieces of Wuxi white silk have been loaded and shipped, stored in various banks, money shops, and warehouses, waiting for the opportunity.

Free Talk

On Morality and Literature

— Youmo Jun

This summer, as the summer vacation was approaching, I received concern from various friends who wrote to inquire about my whereabouts after the summer. They always said that with my moral character and literary talent, the new administration would surely rely on me heavily. However, the outcome did not meet their expectations. So they had to take a step back and write to comfort me, saying that with my moral character and literary talent, there was no need to worry about not being hired. Their kindness is indeed touching; but it could not help but make me greatly doubt the so-called morality and literature.

Estimating a person's morality is inherently as difficult and inaccurate as estimating a student's conduct. Moreover, achieving the level of a "learned person" in literature is also difficult. Furthermore, morality and literature have always been inseparable. I remember reading Zeng Gong's "Letter to Ouyang Sheren" when I was young. Because Ouyang Xiu wrote a tomb inscription for his grandfather Zhiyao, he praised Ouyang Xiu's morality and literature as "appearing only once every few hundred years." However, what exactly was so extraordinary about Ouyang Xiu's morality and literature, even Zeng Gong could not say. This shows how difficult it is to estimate morality and literature. Zeng Gong also divided "human conduct" into five categories: (1) good intentions but bad deeds, (2) treacherous intentions but virtuous appearance, (3) good and evil mixed and cannot be clearly identified, (4) reality greater than reputation, and (5) reputation greater than reality. These five standards seem to be more practical than the five grades of A, B, C, D, and E used in modern schools to estimate students' conduct. However, if I were to use them to estimate my own morality, even I would not know which category I belong to. Even if I were to ask friends to estimate separately, they would probably each give their own estimate, just like teachers grading students' conduct, making it difficult to be accurate. Moreover, these five standards are not true morality!

Therefore, I think: Once one becomes a Chinese literati, it is best to carry a large signboard of "helping the world and guiding education," even though those who have eaten cold pork in the Confucius Temple are few and far between. Precisely because of this, the collections of literati throughout history always contain articles that speak on behalf of the sages or say flattering words to their masters. In this way, one may be worthy of being called "possessing morality and capable of literature." I was born too late, what can I do!

August, 23rd year, on the way to Shaoxing

Dissenting Views on Dissent

— Zhou Muzhai

In today's China, literature, that sort of thing, must be considered the most unlucky. On one side, some people say angrily, "If literature doesn't die, great disasters won't cease!" On the other side, some people say literature is useless.

Perhaps these two sayings can be combined into one, because literature is useless, not as good as science and engineering, which is why great disasters won't cease.

So, some people stand up to defend it. Like Mr. Wang Pingling, he expresses dissent towards the promotion of science and engineering and the cursing of literature, saying that China has been advocating science and engineering for "sixty years," "spending countless tens of millions of gold pounds of the country's scholarship fees," but "no one has ever openly advocated a literary movement, the country has never sacrificed a scholarship fee for literature, and the government has never had the slightest plan for literary facilities." He also believes that "if this continues, Chinese literature will definitely die; however, after literature dies, whether great disasters can cease, this responsibility will have to be completely borne by those who study science and engineering."

We can agree with his defense of literature. However, there are a few dissenting views here that need to be raised.

It is true that the country has never sacrificed a scholarship fee for literature. But one point is not fully expressed, this does not refer to all fees, it does not mean that the country has not sacrificed any fees for literature other than scholarship fees; fees are not limited to scholarship fees. It is half true to say that no one has openly advocated a literary movement. The New Literature Movement in the May Fourth era was openly advocated. After that, it is indeed fair to say that there has been no open advocacy, and "no one knows why." As for saying that the government has never had the slightest plan for literary facilities, this is completely wrong. Perhaps Mr. Wang thinks the plan is "minute," so he didn't see it. In short, the responsibility for such destruction of literature, or at least the responsibility for ignoring literature, cannot be borne by the national government; and it must also be defended on its behalf.

Regarding the country's attitude towards literature, he also cites Hitler's treatment of Hauptmann, Wagner, Mussolini's treatment of D'Annunzio and intellectuals, France's treatment of Rolland, France, such high praise and preferential treatment, as well as the fact that the Soviet Union's leaders are mostly from the literary and artistic circles, and the Japanese Ministry of Education's assistance in the progress of literature and art, to reflect on China's situation, his words filled with emotion and envy. In fact, this is unnecessary; and there is no need for extensive citations, in China, it has "existed since ancient times," which can be understood in general by looking at the two words "civil governance." However, according to China's "national conditions," such active "veneration of literature" only produced many court literatures; on the contrary, works such as Water Margin, Dream of the Red Chamber, and The Scholars were produced outside of this influence. Therefore, we do not expect the country to venerate literature in any way, climbing too high, it is hard to guarantee that it will not fall heavier, it is better to be more plain.

Therefore, finally, returning to the previous article, let's talk about the uselessness of literature and great disasters. But there are only a few words, since literature is considered useless, then even if there is disaster, the disaster of uselessness is not very big.

Illness and Writing

— Xi Dichen

In today's essays and sketches, one often sees texts praising "minor illnesses," saying that minor illnesses are a kind of happiness in life. In addition to getting a little temporary rest from a busy life, it can also allow a heart that is usually tight to relax a bit and fall into a state of light tranquility.

In fact, this peaceful state of mind is most suitable for writing elegant essays. Firstly, the mood during a minor illness is naturally more leisurely, and the observation of surrounding things will be particularly delicate, and it will also seem to feel fresher; secondly, if one inadvertently writes down what one has observed, one will definitely use a light and agile writing style, seemingly just gliding the pen along, without any effort. Good articles can often be obtained at this time, because people are most likely to express "truth" when they are poor and sick.

It is precisely for this reason that articles written during leisure illnesses often make people feel exquisite and lovely, with a fresh flavor. Mr. Yu Dafu's articles are like this. Recently, seeing Mr. Xu Weinan's "Letters from Ji Yun," I couldn't help but have the same feeling.

This collection is a record of the author's stay in Zhapu for a month last year due to a lung illness. (Although it uses the form of letters) The author floats outside of the world, embracing a leisurely mood and child-like interest to observe the mountains, seas, wind, moon, objects, and human feelings of Zhapu, and then writes them down lightly and faintly with a delicate brush, just like a painting, feeling simple and fresh.

The author describes the sea the most. The various postures of the sea in Zhapu on cloudy days and sunny days can be said to be fully captured in the writing. I love the following section the most:

"Watching the sea is a pleasant thing, especially watching the sea at high tide. When the tide rises to the beach, if you look down from the mountain, you can see the tide like pieces stacked on top of each other. One piece of water rushes onto the beach, followed by a second piece of water covering the first piece. This way, one piece covers another, never stopping. Walking down from the mountain to the beach to see the tide is like rolling up, as if it is an unfolding painting, rolling up little by little, and when it reaches the high point of the beach, the painting is rolled up. This is still the scene of the initial high tide, waiting for the high tide (especially on the fourteenth or fifteenth day of the lunar calendar) it is not pieces rushing over, but large chunks leaping over and falling over. When it reaches the beach, it seems extremely angry, jumping up, flying up, roaring loudly, because it is blocked by the stubborn beach, it spits out a pile of white foam and retreats, but then immediately squeezes onto the beach again, as if it must conquer this beach, and later the beach is indeed gradually conquered by the tide. Looking into the distance, the sea water rushing against the edge of the island is like a burst of white smoke. When the sky is illuminated by strong sunlight, the surface of the tide seems to be covered with crystals, rolling over with the crest of the tide, disappearing when it is near the beach. But there is another large pile rolling over in front. Sometimes there are one or two particularly bright spots at the foot of the sea island, like constant lights, always illuminating the sea."

A person's minor illness is truly a person's best rest. In this rest, one can cultivate one's "strength." After reading the above example, one can imagine what great inspiration the author received from the sea.

The author's writing was originally known for its elegance, but now it is even more light and lively.

3 × 2 = 6 People

— TK

Small Scenes of Malay Villages (Part 1)

— Fei Er

Riding a bicycle along the lanes of the tropical forest, one can see scattered villages dotted among the trees along the way.

An "atap" house built on flat ground and raised on wooden stakes, with tropical red-leaf trees, fragrant flowers, and tropical trees planted in the open space in front of the house. The fence in front of the house is painted green, and inside the house, under a kerosene lamp, are reflected some pictures and porcelain plates. Outside the house, coconut trees or betel nut trees extend on the ground. In the outermost layer, bamboo fences or red flowers are used as fences. Every day, one or two workers lazily holding a Javanese tobacco and doing pruning work are the homes of Malay nobles.

Separated by tropical plants, in other parts are the "atap" houses of Malay commoners. The simple wooden boards and the dark tree-leaf roofs weathered by wind and rain show a dim color under the shadows of the trees. Outside the house, the sound of sheep bleating is heard, and a group of chicks are pecking at the weeds. The homeowner holds a "parang" knife and weaves "atap" leaves. When thirsty, he climbs up the tall coconut tree, picks a fruit, climbs down, uses a knife to cut off the fibrous skin, chisels a small hole, and sucks the juice of the pulp inside. That is the "ice cream" or soda of Malay commoners.

On ordinary days, Malay villages exist in an atmosphere of peace and tranquility. The scorching sun filters its light and shadows on the ground through the gaps in the leaves, and the wind sways gently among the trees. There is often a small stream in front of the house, and next to a Malay boat tied up, Malay children are swimming, playing, and passing the days of the scorching sun in the dark red stream water formed by rainwater.

On hot noon and afternoon, a familiar Chinese would stop a bicycle outside the house, mouth facing the homeowner: "Hello, Shuman, (or other Malay name) please give a coconut to quench my thirst."

And the homeowner would jump down from his work, or wake up from a lazy nap, touch the "parang" knife, and say: "Boss, where did you come from? I'll get it for you."

After the guest finished sucking the juice, the car would roll away on the avenue with green grass and golden sunlight. Then the homeowner would hum a love song, playing and singing with a sheepskin drum in his arms.

Or in the tropical rainstorm, the strong wind shakes the surrounding trees, and raindrops hit the "atap" roof in large drops. A coconut oil lamp would be lit in the house, leaving a trace of light and shadow on the dark earth, illuminating the simple furniture in the house, appearing a mess: a few "sarongs," a bag of rice, a bag of sugar, a can of oil in an old wine bottle, and a few sticks of tobacco... (No bed or chair.) If the wind blows away the leaves, the homeowner would climb onto the roof, holding a knife in his hand and leaves in his mouth, drenched by the rain, and repair the house. - Then the tropical rainstorm would pass.

Literary Talk Outside the Door

— Hua Yu

(2) Who Created Characters?

Who created characters?

We are accustomed to hearing that an item was created by a sage in ancient times, and of course we must ask this question about characters. But immediately there is an answer that forgets the origin: characters were created by Cangjie.

This is the view of ordinary scholars, who naturally have their source. I have even seen a portrait of this Cangjie, an old man with four eyes. It can be seen that to create characters, one must have an extraordinary appearance first. People like us with only two eyes are not only not capable enough, but even our appearance is not worthy.

However, the person who wrote the "Book of Changes" (I don't know who it was), was relatively smart. He said, "In ancient times, people governed by knotting ropes; later sages replaced them with writing." He did not say "Cangjie," but only "later sages," did not say creation, but only replacement. He was very cautious; perhaps he inadvertently did not believe that there would be someone in ancient times who created many characters alone, so he just said it vaguely.

But what kind of role were those who used writing to replace knotting ropes? A writer? Yes, judging from the fact that the so-called writers of today are most likely to show off their writing skills, and can do nothing without a pen, one would indeed think of him first; and he should indeed contribute to his own livelihood. However, it is not. People before history, although they sang while working and sang while courting, they did not draft or leave manuscripts, because they never dreamed of selling poems or compiling complete works, and there were no newspapers or bookstores in that society, and writing was useless. According to what some scholars tell us, it is likely that the historian did a lot of work on writing.

In primitive society, there was probably only a witch at first. As things gradually evolved and became more complex, some things, such as sacrifices, hunting, and wars... became necessary to remember, so the witch had no choice but to think of ways to record things in addition to his main job of "inviting spirits." This was the beginning of "history." Moreover, "ascending to heaven," in his official capacity, he also had to burn the records of the chief and the major events under his rule for God to see, so he had to write articles as well -- although this was probably a later development. Later, the responsibilities were divided more clearly, and there were specialized historians. Writing was a necessary tool for historians. The ancients said: "Cangjie was the historian of the Yellow Emperor." The first sentence is not credible, but it points out the relationship between history and writing, which is very interesting. As for the later "writers" who used it to write "Ah, my love, I'm going to die!" those beautiful sentences, that was just enjoying the ready-made, "not worth mentioning"!

Shen Bao Wireless Radio Weekly

Summary of Shortwave Transmitters (2)

— Huang Jiancun

(2) Automatic Transmitters

(1) Practical Oscillation Circuits: The oscillation methods in automatic transmitters can be roughly divided into the following two categories:

(1) Magnetic induction coupling circuit, (2) Capacitance coupling circuit

When designing a transmitter, the choice of circuit is not very important, because the characteristics of the oscillation circuit are often determined by the circuit's fixed value, the vacuum tube used, and adjustments. Therefore, in order to make the transmitter oscillate at a certain frequency, it is necessary to have a matching circuit composed of coils and capacitors.

The most commonly used ones are the Hartley circuit, the tuned plate and tuned grid circuit, and the Colpitts Circuit.

The so-called Hartley circuit, as shown in the upper right figure, has a common coil, one end of the filament is often connected to the center of the coil, and the plate and grid are connected to its two ends. In this way, FG forms a grid circuit, and FP forms a plate circuit. Usually, the number of coil turns on the plate circuit side is more than that on the grid circuit side. Its oscillation effect is determined by the degree of magnetic induction coupling between the two circuits, so it is necessary to pay attention to the ratio of the number of coil turns.

The so-called Colpitts circuit, as shown in the upper left figure, is to remove the self-inductance in the Hartley circuit and replace it with capacitance. In this method, the oscillation effect is determined by the degree of capacitance coupling between the two circuits, so attention should be paid to the ratio of capacitance.

The tuned plate and tuned grid circuit is also known as the Armstrong circuit, named after Mr. E.H. Armstrong, who invented it, as shown in the figure below. In shortwave, this method does not require external coupling, and the electrical energy in the plate circuit is returned to the grid circuit through the internal capacitance of the vacuum tube to maintain the oscillation state.

Transmitter Efficiency and Frequency Stability Issues

— Shi Huayu

At present, amateur radio operators in our country are also gradually leaning towards shortwave. The most interesting thing about studying shortwave is making small-power transmitters. The most important thing to pay attention to in a transmitter is how to stabilize the frequency. And because the power is small, efficiency must also be taken into account. Now I will describe these two key points in detail below:

The frequency stability and efficiency of a transmitter are related to each other, although the conditions most suitable for stabilizing the frequency are not necessarily suitable for achieving its highest efficiency in a certain circuit. However, it is generally believed that stabilizing the frequency of a transmitter is the most important issue in the design of a transmitter. The most ideal transmitter should always emit a signal on one frequency, and it should only occupy a minimum position in the high-frequency band. Especially because its electrical energy is completely concentrated on one frequency, it can exert the greatest power. If we pay a little attention when receiving radio, we can find that many radio stations occupy many degrees on the dial, or sometimes although they do not occupy many degrees, they often jump from one degree to another; at the same time, their signals are often blurred and rough. These radio stations do not have ideal frequencies, and they do not have the most stable frequencies.

The reasons for these unstable frequencies can be roughly divided into two categories. The first category is mechanical defects, and the second category is dynamic defects.

Mechanical changes and heating of the transmitter structure can often cause mechanical instability of frequency. For example, changes in the space between the plates of the storage capacitor, changes in the distance between the turns of the coil, and changes in the distance between the electrodes of the vacuum tube can all cause the transmitter frequency to sway. As long as we fix the structure of each part during manufacturing and installation, the above defects can be easily avoided. The change in the distance between the poles of the vacuum tube due to temperature changes, which causes a considerable change in capacitance, is also a reason for frequency sway. The frequency instability caused by this reason can also be avoided by using the vacuum tube's specified power a little less.

Dynamic instability is closely related to the total impedance of the vacuum tube. When transmitting, a change in the total impedance of the plate circuit will greatly affect the frequency. Unstable plate voltage of the transmitter can cause frequency changes. Therefore, it is best not to use a power supply with poor filtering. At the same time, the transmitter should also avoid excessive or insufficient excitation, so the grid excitation voltage or grid leak should be kept at the most suitable value. The best way to avoid dynamic instability is to pay attention to the values of each item in the circuit design and keep them unchanged.

The nature of the transmitter load circuit (including the plate circuit and antenna circuit) and the loss of the grid circuit have a significant relationship to the transmitter efficiency. The so-called plate efficiency refers to the ratio of high-frequency power output to plate input. When calculating the actual overall efficiency of the transmitter, the power consumed on the filament side must also be calculated. Sometimes the loss on the grid circuit side is very large, and the reason is that the grid leak loss is too large or because high-frequency current passes through the grid and filament. The latter can be considered to be due to the excessive capacitance between the grid and filament when the frequency is very high.

For oscillation tubes with extremely high frequencies, it is quite difficult for us to calculate its plate efficiency. However, when the oscillation tube is under regular plate power consumption (usually when the plate is somewhat red), the power output is approximately close to the difference between the plate power input in watts (i.e., DC plate voltage multiplied by plate current in amperes) and the specified plate consumption in watts. To ask for a more accurate value, it is of course necessary to subtract the power consumed by the grid leak. The power consumed by the grid leak is the grid leak resistance multiplied by the square of the grid current.

In short, transmitter efficiency and frequency stability are the most important issues in shortwave transmission, and also the most difficult issues to solve. Using purely calculation methods to investigate will often be further from reality; obviously, it also requires you to expend a lot of brainpower!
